Prophethood
beginner
5 min
Proof of Prophethood: The Role of Miracles
Sanusi opens the chapter on proof of messengers, defines sending messengers as possible, and gives an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sending messengers is rationally possible for God, and that miracles serve as divine attestation to their truthfulness, illustrated by the royal assembly example.

Core Idea
Miracles are God’s direct endorsement of a prophet’s message, like a king’s hidden confirmation.

This lesson opens the chapter on prophethood. Sanusi first establishes that sending messengers is among the possible acts of God. Then he explains that miracles function as God’s guarantee of the prophet’s truthfulness, replacing a direct divine statement. Finally, he begins a famous analogy: a king hidden from his subjects sends a messenger to deliver a warning. Though the example is cut short, the core idea is clear — the miracle is the king’s sign that the messenger is trustworthy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: definition of possibility, then explanation of miracles, then the example.
The passage ends mid-sentence in the example; focus on the established concepts.
2
Understand the concept of 'possible'
Sanusi says sending messengers is among the possible things (ja'izat). Consider why this is important: it means God is not obligated to send messengers, but it is rationally permissible.
This grounds the discussion in necessary, possible, impossible categories.
3
Grasp the role of miracles
Miracles indicate the messenger's truthfulness, taking the place of God directly saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' How does this analogy work?
The miracle is a sign from God that confirms the message.
4
Analyze the royal assembly example
Read the example of the person claiming to speak for a hidden king. How does this illustrate the function of a miracle? What does the king do to verify the messenger?
The example is incomplete, but the teaching point is clear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الدليل على ثبوت رسالة الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام عموماً وعلی ثبوت رسالة نبينا و مولانا محمد صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم خصوصاً و بیان وجه دلالته المعجزة ، وتقريرها بالمثال
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ : بعثُهُ سبحانَهُ رُسُلَهُ للعبادِ ليبلغوهم أمر الله تعالى ونهيه وإباحته وما يتعلَّق بذلكَ ، وأَيَّدَهم سبحانه فضلاً منه بما يدلُّ على صِدْقِهم فيما بلغوا عنه ؛ بحيث يتنزَّلُ ذلكَ منزلة قولِهِ تعالى : صَدَقَ عبدي في كلِّ ما يُبلغ عني .
وقد مثَّلَ ذلكَ أئمَّتُنا رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم بشخص ادَّعى في محفل عظيم بمجلس ملك والملك قد حجب الجميع عن مشاهدتِهِ ، فقال الشخص : أتعرفونَ لِمَ جمعَكمُ الملك ؟ جمعكم ليأمركم بكذا وينهاكم عن كذا ، ويُعلمكم بأنَّكم قدِ استقبلْتُم هَوْلاً جسيماً ، وأمراً تذوبُ العقولُ والأكباد والقلوبُ بمُجرَّدِ سماعِهِ ، وكَرْباً يمنعُ نومَ العقلاء عظيماً ، لا يسلم منه إلا
Chapter: The proof of the establishment of the message of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, generally, and of the establishment of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, specifically, and an explanation of the aspect of its evidence, the miracle, and its exposition by example.
And among the possible things: His sending, glorified be He, His messengers to the servants to convey to them the command of God, the Exalted, and His prohibition and His permission and what pertains to that; and He supported them, glorified be He, as a favor from Him, with what indicates their truthfulness in what they conveyed from Him; such that that takes the place of His statement, the Exalted: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me.'
And our imams, may God be pleased with them, gave an example of that by a person who claimed in a great assembly in the court of a king, and the king had veiled everyone from seeing him, so the person said: 'Do you know why the king gathered you? He gathered you to command you such-and-such, forbid you such-and-such, and inform you that you have encountered a great terror, and a matter at whose mere hearing intellects, livers, and hearts melt, and a great distress that prevents the sleep of the wise, from which no one is safe except...'
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage opens a new chapter on the proof of prophethood. It first establishes the general proof for all messengers and specifically for Prophet Muhammad. The proof is the miracle (mu'jizah), and how it provides evidence. Sanusi then states that sending messengers is among the possible (ja'izat) acts of God. They are sent to convey His commands, prohibitions, permissions, and related matters. God supports them with miracles that indicate their truthfulness, such that the miracle takes the place of God directly saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully in all he conveys from Me.' Then Sanusi gives an example from the imams: a person in a great assembly at a king's court, where the king is hidden from view, claims to speak on the king's behalf. The person asks if the people know why the king gathered them, and then explains the king's command, prohibition, and warning of a great terror and distress. The example illustrates how the miracle serves as a confirmation from the king (God) that the messenger is truthful, even though the king is not seen or heard directly. The passage ends mid-sentence with 'from which no one is safe except...' likely continuing the warning in the example.

Key Terms
رسالة
رسل
معجزة
بعث
جائز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are just extraordinary events that prove a prophet has supernatural powers.
Correction: Sanusi explains that miracles are not merely extraordinary; they are a divine attestation that takes the place of God directly affirming the messenger's truthfulness.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what purpose do miracles serve in relation to messengers?
A) They prove that messengers have supernatural powers.
B) They indicate the truthfulness of the messengers, taking the place of God's direct statement.
C) They demonstrate that messengers are divine themselves.
D) They are merely to attract followers.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are God's confirmation of a prophet's truthfulness, functioning as a direct statement from God that the prophet is honest.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The example speaks of a 'great terror' and 'great distress that prevents the sleep of the wise.' Do you lie awake at night with the reality of the Day of Judgment, or have worldly concerns drowned out that warning? What one change in your daily routine would make that terror feel real to you again?
?
If the miracle is equivalent to God saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me,' then every command of the Prophet is a direct message from God. Where in your life are you treating a prophetic teaching as optional or negotiable? What would it look like to obey that teaching today as if God Himself just whispered it to you?
?
The king was veiled, and the people could not see or hear him directly. Yet the messenger's claim was confirmed by the king's hidden sign. Do you live with that same certainty about the unseen God and His messengers? When doubts arise about the truth of prophethood, what concrete reminder from this lesson can you bring to mind to restore your conviction?

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Rational Proof of Prophethood
Sanusi states the proof of prophethood and the evidential role of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the possibility of prophethood and the evidence of miracles constitute a rational proof that a prophet is truthful.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's signature verifying a messenger's truth.

Sanusi introduces the proof of prophethood by first establishing that sending messengers is rationally possible (jā'iz). He then explains that God supports them with miracles, which serve as direct divine attestation of their truthfulness. This passage lays the foundation for understanding why miracles are not just wonders but essential proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing, then read the translation. Notice the structure: first a general statement about prophethood, then the specific role of miracles.
The phrase 'صَدَقَ عبدي' is crucial—it shows miracles take the place of God's own testimony.
2
Identify the two key claims
Find where Sanusi states that sending messengers is among contingent things (جائزات), and where he explains that miracles function as divine confirmation of truth.
3
Reflect on the logic
Ask yourself: Why does the fact that miracles are like God saying 'My servant is truthful' prove prophethood? Consider how miracles are beyond human power and point to divine intervention.
This is the core of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الدليل على ثبوت رسالة الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام عموماً وعلی ثبوت رسالة نبينا و مولانا محمت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم خصوصاً و بیان وجه دلالته المعجزة ، وتقريرها بالمثال
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ : بعثُهُ سبحانَهُ رُسُلَهُ للعبادِ ليبلغوهم أمر الله تعالى ونهيه وإباحته وما يتعلَّق بذلكَ ، وأَيَّدَهم سبحانه فضلاً منه بما يدلُّ على صِدْقِهم فيما بلغوا عنه ؛ بحيث يتنزَّلُ ذلكَ منزلة قولِهِ تعالى : صَدَقَ عبدي في كلِّ [سو؟] ما يُبلغ عني .
وقد مثَّلَ ذلكَ أئمَّتُنا رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم بشخص ادَّعى في محفل عظيم بمجلس ملك والملك قد حجب الجميع عن مشاهدتِهِ ، فقال الشخص : أتعرفونَ لِمَ جمعَكمُ الملك ؟ جمعكم ليأمركم بكذا وينهاكم عن كذا ، ويُعلمكم بأنَّكم قدِ استقبلْتُم هَوْلاً جسيماً ، وأمراً تذوبُ العقولُ والأكباد والقلوبُ بمُجرَّدِ سماعِهِ ، وكَرْباً يمنعُ نومَ العقلاء عظيماً ، لا يسلم منه إلا مَنْ بادرَ الآنَ للاستعدادِ لهُ قبلَ هجومه ، وألقى السمع وأحضرَ كلَّ الفكرِ لما يشيرُ عليهِ الملك في ذلكَ مِنْ مكنون علومه . وقد أمرني بتبليغ ذلك إليكمُ الآنَ ، فالبدارَ البِدارَ ؛ إِذْ ليسَ بينكم وبينَ ذلكَ الأمرِ المَخُوفِ إِلا القليلُ مِنَ الزمانِ ، وأنا لكم بينَ يَدَيْ ذلكَ الهولِ الناصحُ الأمينُ والنذيرُ العُرْيانُ . وقد أنهيتُ إليكم رسالة الملكِ ؛ فمَنْ أطاعَهُ ، وأحسنَ النظر لنفسِهِ . . فقد استخلصها ، واغتنم عظيمَ رضاه ، ومَنْ عصاه ، وأهملَ النظر لنفسِهِ .. فقد تعرَّضَ لما لا يُطاقُ مِنْ هول سخط الملكِ ، ولا أحد يطيقُ إنقاذَهُ مِنْ عظيمٍ رَدَاهُ وقولي هذا تعلمون أنَّهُ بِعِلْمٍ مِنَ الملكِ ومرأى منهُ الآنَ وإِنَّهُ وإِنْ حَجَبَنا الآن عن مشاهدته فليس هو ومَسْمَعِ محجوباً عن رؤيتنا وسماع ما يجري بيننا ، وهو الذي يضعُ مَنْ يشاءُ ويرفعُ ، وهو القادرُ أنْ يعاقبني إِنْ كَذبتُ عنه ولا ملجأ لي إن عصيته ولا مهرب لي ولا مدفع . وقد عهدتُمونى من لدن نشأتي : لا أسمح لنفسي بكذبة على مَنْ هو مثلي وعلى شاكلتي ، وإن نفعتني وأمنَتْ فيها مِنْ كلِّ ضررٍ ناحيتي ، فكيف أتجاسر بعدما تكامل عقلي ونقصت صبوتي ، واشتعل الشيب في صدغي ولحيتي.
Chapter: The proof of the establishment of the message of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, in general, and the establishment of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, in particular, and the explanation of the aspect of its evidence — the miracle — and its confirmation by example.
And among possible things is His sending, exalted be He, His messengers to the servants to convey to them the command of God, His prohibition, His permission, and what pertains to that. And He supported them, exalted be He, as a favor from Him, with what indicates their truthfulness in what they conveyed from Him; such that this takes the place of His saying: 'My servant has spoken truly in everything he conveys from Me.'
And our imams, may God be pleased with them, illustrated that with a person who claimed in a great gathering in the court of a king, while the king had veiled everyone from seeing him. The person said: 'Do you know why the king gathered you? He gathered you to command you with such-and-such and forbid you from such-and-such, and to inform you that you have encountered a tremendous terror, a matter at the mere hearing of which minds, livers, and hearts melt, and a great distress that prevents the sleep of the intelligent, from which none will be saved except those who now hasten to prepare for it before its attack, and lend ear and bring all thought to what the king indicates concerning that from his hidden knowledge. He has commanded me to convey that to you now, so hasten, hasten; for there is between you and that fearful matter only a little time. And I am, before that terror, your sincere adviser, faithful warner, and bare warner. I have conveyed to you the king's message: so whoever obeys him and considers well for himself — he has saved himself and gained his great pleasure; and whoever disobeys him and neglects consideration for himself — he has exposed himself to an intolerable horror of the king's anger, and no one can rescue him from his great ruin. And this statement of mine — you know that it is with the king's knowledge and sight now, and that although he has veiled us now from seeing him, he is not veiled from seeing us and hearing what transpires among us. He is the one who abases whom He wills and exalts, and He is powerful to punish me if I lie about him, and I have no refuge if I disobey him, no escape and no defense. And you have known me from my upbringing: I do not allow myself a lie concerning someone like me and of my kind, even if it benefits me and I am secure from all harm on my part. So how would I dare, after my intellect has matured and my passion has diminished, and gray hair has appeared in my temples and beard?'
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a proof and illustration in the context of establishing prophethood. The author first states that among the contingent (jā'izāt) things is God's sending of messengers to convey His commands, prohibitions, and permissions. God supports them with miracles (mu‘jizāt) that take the place of His direct statement that the messenger is truthful. Then the author provides a detailed parable (tamthīl) by the imams to clarify this: a person appears before a crowd in a king's court, the king being hidden from sight. The person explains that the king has gathered them for a serious matter, and he (the person) is relaying the king's message. He warns them of impending danger and urges immediate obedience. He emphasizes that the king sees and hears everything, and that he (the messenger) would never dare to lie, especially now that he is mature and old, and that he has a reputation for truthfulness even in minor matters. The parable is meant to illustrate how the miracle (the messenger's evident truthfulness and the coherence of his message) functions as a sign from God, analogous to the king's knowledge of the messenger's actions. The passage follows the order: first the general principle, then the concrete example that makes the abstract concept tangible.

Key Terms
جائزات
معجزة
بعثة
رسالة
صدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophethood can only be known by direct revelation to oneself, not by rational evidence.
Correction: Sanusi shows that rational possibility (jā'iz) and the evidence of miracles provide a rational proof for the truth of a prophet.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi compare miracles to in terms of their evidential value?
A) A king's direct command
B) God's own statement that the messenger is truthful
C) A logical argument from contingency
D) The messenger's personal charisma

Key Takeaway
The possibility of prophethood and the evidence of miracles form a rational foundation for believing in a messenger's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was sent by God, or do you just believe because you were born into a Muslim family? This lesson says miracles are God's testimony for the messenger. Have you ever personally examined the miracle of the Quran as evidence? If not, are you willing to do so now, and let that proof shape your conviction?
?
The source says miracles take the place of God saying 'My servant has spoken truly.' If you heard God say that directly about the Prophet, would you obey every command of the sunnah without hesitation? If you find yourself picking and choosing which aspects of Islam to follow, what does that say about your acceptance of the Prophet's truthfulness?
?
Prophethood is described as 'possible' but not necessary. Could God have left humanity without guidance? He did not. Should this not fill your heart with gratitude that He sent messengers? Have you thanked Him today for the gift of prophethood and the miracle that confirms it? If not, what is holding you back from a deeper appreciation of this blessing?

Prophethood

The Parable of the King's Messenger
Sanusi presents the imams' parable illustrating how miracles authenticate prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the parable of the king's messenger illustrates the role of miracles in verifying prophethood.

Core Idea
A prophet's truthfulness is confirmed by his character and the miracle, just as a trusted messenger is believed.

To make the abstract proof concrete, the imams gave a parable of a messenger in a king's court. The king is hidden, and the messenger delivers a warning. The messenger's credibility is established by his personal truthfulness and the king's unseen awareness. This mirrors how a prophet's miracle and his integrity attest to his divine mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the parable from start to finish
Read the entire Arabic passage of the parable once, then read the translation. Imagine the scene: a gathering, a hidden king, a messenger warning of imminent danger.
2
Identify the key elements
List the main characters: the king, the messenger, the audience. What is the message? What is the threat? How does the messenger prove his trustworthiness?
3
Map to prophethood
Reflect on how each element corresponds to God (the King), the prophet (the messenger), humanity (the audience), the divine message, and the miracle (the messenger's reliability and the king's knowledge).
The miracle is analogous to the messenger's lifelong truthfulness and the king's unseen surveillance.
4
Appreciate the logic
Consider why the parable is effective: it shows that the messenger's trustworthiness is enough to confirm his message, just as the miracle confirms the prophet's truth. The miracle is not just a trick but a sign of divine endorsement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الدليل على ثبوت رسالة الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام عموماً وعلی ثبوت رسالة نبينا و مولانا محمت صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم خصوصاً و بیان وجه دلالته المعجزة ، وتقريرها بالمثال
ومِنَ الجائزاتِ : بعثُهُ سبحانَهُ رُسُلَهُ للعبادِ ليبلغوهم أمر الله تعالى ونهيه وإباحته وما يتعلَّق بذلكَ ، وأَيَّدَهم سبحانه فضلاً منه بما يدلُّ على صِدْقِهم فيما بلغوا عنه ؛ بحيث يتنزَّلُ ذلكَ منزلة قولِهِ تعالى : صَدَقَ عبدي في كلِّ [سو؟] ما يُبلغ عني .
وقد مثَّلَ ذلكَ أئمَّتُنا رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنهم بشخص ادَّعى في محفل عظيم بمجلس ملك والملك قد حجب الجميع عن مشاهدتِهِ ، فقال الشخص : أتعرفونَ لِمَ جمعَكمُ الملك ؟ جمعكم ليأمركم بكذا وينهاكم عن كذا ، ويُعلمكم بأنَّكم قدِ استقبلْتُم هَوْلاً جسيماً ، وأمراً تذوبُ العقولُ والأكباد والقلوبُ بمُجرَّدِ سماعِهِ ، وكَرْباً يمنعُ نومَ العقلاء عظيماً ، لا يسلم منه إلا مَنْ بادرَ الآنَ للاستعدادِ لهُ قبلَ هجومه ، وألقى السمع وأحضرَ كلَّ الفكرِ لما يشيرُ عليهِ الملك في ذلكَ مِنْ مكنون علومه . وقد أمرني بتبليغ ذلك إليكمُ الآنَ ، فالبدارَ البِدارَ ؛ إِذْ ليسَ بينكم وبينَ ذلكَ الأمرِ المَخُوفِ إِلا القليلُ مِنَ الزمانِ ، وأنا لكم بينَ يَدَيْ ذلكَ الهولِ الناصحُ الأمينُ والنذيرُ العُرْيانُ . وقد أنهيتُ إليكم رسالة الملكِ ؛ فمَنْ أطاعَهُ ، وأحسنَ النظر لنفسِهِ . . فقد استخلصها ، واغتنم عظيمَ رضاه ، ومَنْ عصاه ، وأهملَ النظر لنفسِهِ .. فقد تعرَّضَ لما لا يُطاقُ مِنْ هول سخط الملكِ ، ولا أحد يطيقُ إنقاذَهُ مِنْ عظيمٍ رَدَاهُ وقولي هذا تعلمون أنَّهُ بِعِلْمٍ مِنَ الملكِ ومرأى منهُ الآنَ وإِنَّهُ وإِنْ حَجَبَنا الآن عن مشاهدته فليس هو ومَسْمَعِ محجوباً عن رؤيتنا وسماع ما يجري بيننا ، وهو الذي يضعُ مَنْ يشاءُ ويرفعُ ، وهو القادرُ أنْ يعاقبني إِنْ كَذبتُ عنه ولا ملجأ لي إن عصيته ولا مهرب لي ولا مدفع . وقد عهدتُمونى من لدن نشأتي : لا أسمح لنفسي بكذبة على مَنْ هو مثلي وعلى شاكلتي ، وإن نفعتني وأمنَتْ فيها مِنْ كلِّ ضررٍ ناحيتي ، فكيف أتجاسر بعدما تكامل عقلي ونقصت صبوتي ، واشتعل الشيب في صدغي ولحيتي.
Chapter: The proof of the establishment of the message of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, in general, and the establishment of the message of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, in particular, and the explanation of the aspect of its evidence — the miracle — and its confirmation by example.
And among possible things is His sending, exalted be He, His messengers to the servants to convey to them the command of God, His prohibition, His permission, and what pertains to that. And He supported them, exalted be He, as a favor from Him, with what indicates their truthfulness in what they conveyed from Him; such that this takes the place of His saying: 'My servant has spoken truly in everything he conveys from Me.'
And our imams, may God be pleased with them, illustrated that with a person who claimed in a great gathering in the court of a king, while the king had veiled everyone from seeing him. The person said: 'Do you know why the king gathered you? He gathered you to command you with such-and-such and forbid you from such-and-such, and to inform you that you have encountered a tremendous terror, a matter at the mere hearing of which minds, livers, and hearts melt, and a great distress that prevents the sleep of the intelligent, from which none will be saved except those who now hasten to prepare for it before its attack, and lend ear and bring all thought to what the king indicates concerning that from his hidden knowledge. He has commanded me to convey that to you now, so hasten, hasten; for there is between you and that fearful matter only a little time. And I am, before that terror, your sincere adviser, faithful warner, and bare warner. I have conveyed to you the king's message: so whoever obeys him and considers well for himself — he has saved himself and gained his great pleasure; and whoever disobeys him and neglects consideration for himself — he has exposed himself to an intolerable horror of the king's anger, and no one can rescue him from his great ruin. And this statement of mine — you know that it is with the king's knowledge and sight now, and that although he has veiled us now from seeing him, he is not veiled from seeing us and hearing what transpires among us. He is the one who abases whom He wills and exalts, and He is powerful to punish me if I lie about him, and I have no refuge if I disobey him, no escape and no defense. And you have known me from my upbringing: I do not allow myself a lie concerning someone like me and of my kind, even if it benefits me and I am secure from all harm on my part. So how would I dare, after my intellect has matured and my passion has diminished, and gray hair has appeared in my temples and beard?'
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage is a proof and illustration in the context of establishing prophethood. The author first states that among the contingent (jā'izāt) things is God's sending of messengers to convey His commands, prohibitions, and permissions. God supports them with miracles (mu‘jizāt) that take the place of His direct statement that the messenger is truthful. Then the author provides a detailed parable (tamthīl) by the imams to clarify this: a person appears before a crowd in a king's court, the king being hidden from sight. The person explains that the king has gathered them for a serious matter, and he (the person) is relaying the king's message. He warns them of impending danger and urges immediate obedience. He emphasizes that the king sees and hears everything, and that he (the messenger) would never dare to lie, especially now that he is mature and old, and that he has a reputation for truthfulness even in minor matters. The parable is meant to illustrate how the miracle (the messenger's evident truthfulness and the coherence of his message) functions as a sign from God, analogous to the king's knowledge of the messenger's actions. The passage follows the order: first the general principle, then the concrete example that makes the abstract concept tangible.

Key Terms
تمثيل
صدق
ناصح
أمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The parable is a historical event that actually happened with a specific king.
Correction: The imams use it as a logical analogy (tamthīl) to explain the proof, not as a report of a real incident.

Checkpoint
What reason does the messenger give for the audience to believe that his warning is genuine?
A) He shows them a miraculous sign from the king
B) He reminds them of his lifelong habit of truthfulness and that the king is watching
C) He offers them a reward if they obey
D) He threatens them with immediate punishment

Key Takeaway
The parable makes clear that a prophet's truthfulness is confirmed by his entire life and the miracle, just as the king's messenger relied on his reputation and the king's omniscience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The messenger says he never lied even for personal gain. In what area of your life do you most often excuse small lies for your own benefit? How does this parable force you to reconsider that?
?
You know God is all-aware, just as the king in the parable. Yet how often do you act as if your sins are hidden? What would change if you truly believed God sees every act?
?
The messenger's message was urgent—there is little time. If you truly believed that death could come at any moment, what is one thing you would change today? Why haven't you changed it yet?

The Messenger's Twofold Proof: Character and Miracle
Allegorical proof of prophethood through character and miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how kalam argues for a prophet's truthfulness using both impeccable character and the performance of miracles as the ultimate proof.

Core Idea
A messenger proves his truthfulness first by character, then by miracle.

This passage presents a vivid allegory of a messenger sent by a king to warn the people. The messenger appeals to his lifelong honesty and sincerity, and then offers to ask the king for a miracle if doubts remain. This mirrors the classical kalam proof for prophethood, where a prophet's character and miracle together establish his truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the allegory
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the messenger builds his case step by step.
2
Identify the character-based proof
The messenger points to his known honesty, maturity, and lack of self-interest. Why is this a strong argument?
The messenger argues it is inconceivable he would lie about the king given his character and the king's power.
3
Recognize the miracle as final proof
When character evidence may not suffice, the messenger offers to request a miracle (breaking habit). This is the conclusive proof.
The miracle cuts off all excuse and produces necessary knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَنْ بادرَ الآنَ للاستعدادِ لهُ قبلَ هجومه ، وألقى السمع وأحضرَ كلَّ الفكرِ لما يشيرُ عليهِ الملك في ذلكَ مِنْ مكنون علومه . وقد أمرني بتبليغ ذلك إليكمُ الآنَ ، فالبدارَ البِدارَ ؛ إِذْ ليسَ بينكم وبينَ ذلكَ الأمرِ المَخُوفِ إِلا القليلُ مِنَ الزمانِ ، وأنا لكم بينَ يَدَيْ ذلكَ الهولِ الناصحُ الأمينُ والنذيرُ العُرْيانُ . وقد أنهيتُ إليكم رسالة الملكِ ؛ فمَنْ أطاعَهُ ، وأحسنَ النظر لنفسِهِ . . فقد استخلصها ، واغتنم عظيمَ رضاه ، ومَنْ عصاه ، وأهملَ النظر لنفسِهِ .. فقد تعرَّضَ لما لا يُطاقُ مِنْ هول سخط الملكِ ، ولا أحد يطيقُ إنقاذَهُ مِنْ عظيمٍ رَدَاهُ وقولي هذا تعلمون أنَّهُ بِعِلْمٍ مِنَ الملكِ ومرأى منهُ الآنَ وإِنَّهُ وإِنْ حَجَبَنا الآن عن مشاهدته فليس هو [؟] ومَسْمَعِ محجوباً عن رؤيتنا وسماع ما يجري بيننا ، وهو الذي يضعُ مَنْ يشاءُ ويرفعُ ، وهو القادرُ أنْ يعاقبني إِنْ كَذبتُ عنه ولا ملجأ لي إن عصيته ولا مهرب لي ولا مدفع . وقد عهدتُمونى من لدن نشأتي : لا أسمح لنفسي بكذبة على مَنْ هو مثلي وعلى شاكلتي ، وإن نفعتني وأمنَتْ فيها مِنْ كلِّ ضررٍ ناحيتي ، فكيف أتجاسر بعدما تكامل عقلي ونقصت صبوتي ، واشتعل الشيب في صدغي ولحيتي . على أنْ أكذب على الملكِ بمرأى منهُ ومَسْمَعِ ، مع علمي بعظيم سطوتِهِ وقهرِهِ ، وأليم عقوبتِهِ لَمَنْ تَعَرَّضَ لجنابِهِ العلي واستخف بعظيم أمرِه ؟! فأي سماء تظلُّني ، وأي أرض تقلُّني .. إن كذبتُ عنه حرفاً ؟! وأنا أتحقَّقُ أني لو تقوَّلْتُ عليهِ بعض الأقاويل ، وفُهْتُ لكم عنهُ خُلْفاً . . لأخذ مني باليمين ، ولقطع مني الوتين ، ولا أجد منكم أحداً عنِّي حاجزين . ثم إن لم يقنعكم هذا في تحققِ صِدْقِ مقالتي ، واستربتُم فيَّ معَ ما جرَّبْتُمُ التجريب التام مِنْ كمال نصحي لكم ، وشدَّةِ رأفتي بكم ، وعظيم شفقتي ، وشَرَفِ سابقتي ، وتنزهي عن كل رذيلة ، خصوصاً رذيلة الكذب وما تتحققونَ مِنْ حُسْنِ سيرتي.. فهنا ما يقطعُ العذر لكلِّ أحدٍ ، وتطلعُ به شموس المعرفة الضرورية على آفاقِ القلوب حتى لا ينكرها إلا مَنْ تعرَّضَ لسخط الملكِ وحقَّتْ عليه كلمةُ العذابِ فعاندَ وجَحَدَ ؛ وذلكَ أَنْ أَسأَلَ الملك كما تفضَّلَ ببعثي إليكم لبيان مراشدكم وإنذاركم قبل هجوم ما يفوتُ معَهُ استعدادكم لمعادِكم.. يتفضَّلُ أيضاً بإبانة صدقي فيما عنهُ بلَّغْتُ ، وأنّي ما كذبتُ عنه وما نَزَغْتُ ؛ بأنْ يخرقَ عادتَهُ ، ويفعل كذا وكذا ممَّا ليسَ
Whoever now hastens to prepare for it before its attack, and lends ear and brings all his thought to what the king points to him of the hidden sciences. And he has commanded me to convey that to you now, so hasten, hasten; for there is not between you and that fearful matter except a little time, and I am for you before that terror, the sincere advisor and the naked warner. And I have conveyed to you the message of the king; so whoever obeys him and considers well for himself, he has saved it and gained his great pleasure; and whoever disobeys him and neglects consideration for himself, he has exposed himself to the unbearable terror of the king's wrath, and no one can rescue him from his great destruction. And this my saying – you know that it is with the king's knowledge and sight now, and that although he has veiled us now from seeing him, he is not hidden from our sight and hearing of what transpires between us, and He is the one who abases whom He wills and exalts, and He is able to punish me if I lie about Him, and there is no refuge for me if I disobey Him, nor any escape, nor any defense. And you have known me from my upbringing: I do not permit myself a lie against one like me and of my kind, even if it benefits me and I am safe from all harm on my part; so how could I dare, after my mind reached completion and my youth diminished, and gray hair spread in my temples and beard, to lie against the king in his sight and hearing, while knowing the greatness of his power and force, and the painful punishment of his for whoever affronts his lofty presence and makes light of his great command?! What heaven could shade me, and what earth could carry me, if I lied about him a single letter?! And I verify that if I had fabricated some sayings against him, and uttered to you contrary to what he said, he would seize me by the right hand and cut my aorta, and you would not find any one to be a barrier from me. Then if this does not convince you of the truth of my statement, and you are in doubt about me, despite your perfect experience of my complete sincere advice to you, my intense compassion for you, my great sympathy, the honor of my precedence, and my being free from every vice, especially the vice of lying, and what you know of my good conduct – here is that which cuts off the excuse for everyone, and by which the suns of necessary knowledge rise on the horizons of hearts, so that none deny it except one who exposes himself to the king's wrath and the word of punishment becomes due to him, so he is obstinate and denies; and that is that I ask the king – just as he favored by sending me to you to explain your guidance and warn you before the attack of that which with it your preparation for your return would be missed – he also favors by manifesting my truthfulness in what I have conveyed from him, and that I did not lie about him nor fabricate; by that he breaks his habit and does such and such which is not ...
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is a dramatic narrative allegory illustrating the proof of a messenger's truthfulness, which parallels the kalam proof for prophethood. The messenger (symbolizing a prophet) begins by urging immediate preparation for the king's (God's) judgment, emphasizing the urgency. He establishes his credibility by identifying himself as the 'sincere advisor' and 'naked warner' (one who warns without fear). Then he appeals to the people's knowledge that his message is given openly with the king's awareness, and although the king is invisible, he sees and hears all. The messenger argues that his own truthfulness is proven by his lifelong habit of never lying even when it was safe, so now with mature age and wisdom it is even less conceivable that he would lie about the king, given the king's power to punish him immediately. He vividly describes the impossibility of escape if he lied. Finally, he offers a clinching argument: if all this character evidence is insufficient, he will ask the king to perform a miracle (break his habit) to confirm his truthfulness. This is the classic kalam argument that prophets are known by their impeccable moral character and that the final proof of their truthfulness is the miracle they perform.

النذير العريان
خرق العادة

معرفة ضرورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A prophet's truthfulness is established solely by his character and sincerity.
Correction: While character is a strong indication, the ultimate proof is a miracle (breaking of habit) that confirms his message.

Checkpoint
What does the messenger propose to do if the people still doubt his truthfulness?
A) Punish them
B) Ask the king to perform a miracle (break his habit)
C) Present more writings
D) Leave them

Key Takeaway
The truthfulness of a prophet is proven first by impeccable character and then definitively by the miracle he performs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read the messenger's argument that his lifelong truthfulness makes it impossible for him to lie about God. Look at your own life: are there small compromises with honesty—little exaggerations or convenient untruths—that you tolerate? How can you change that today, starting now?
?
The messenger offers a miracle to the obstinate. If you were to witness a clear, undeniable miracle, would you submit immediately, or would you, like the obstinate, find a reason to explain it away? What is in your heart that might resist even the most obvious sign?
?
The messenger says that the king sees and hears everything. When you sin in private, do you truly feel that you are in the presence of God, or do you act as if He does not see? What one practice can you adopt today to cultivate constant awareness of His sight?

Proof of Prophetic Truthfulness through Miracles
Sanusi proves prophetic truthfulness using a rational analogy of a messenger before a king.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the occurrence of miracles serves as a rational proof for the truthfulness of prophets, using the analogy of a king confirming his messenger.

Core Idea
A miracle is God's authentication of a prophet, just as a king's extraordinary act confirms his messenger.

Sanusi presents a compelling rational analogy to demonstrate why miracles are not merely wondrous events but divine confirmations of prophecy. By imagining a messenger before a powerful king, he shows that only a truthful messenger would dare to ask for a miraculous sign, and the king's granting of it proves the messenger's honesty. This passage then applies the analogy directly to the prophets, establishing that their miracles are God's testimony to their truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall story. Then read the translation. Notice the messenger's reasoning and the test proposed.
The analogy is detailed; Pay attention to the messenger's claims about his own character.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the roles: the king, the messenger, the audience, and the miracle (breaking of custom). Understand how each element contributes to the proof.
The messenger asks the king to do something extraordinary to verify his message.
3
Understand the logical inference
The king's response is equivalent to a direct declaration of the messenger's truthfulness. Learn why this inference is necessary (daruri) for those present or who hear via tawatur.
This establishes the principle of miraculous confirmation.
4
Apply to the prophets
Sanusi explicitly states that the same logic applies to prophets. Reflect on how miracles serve as divine endorsements.
The prophets' character also supports their truthfulness, but the miracle is the decisive proof.
5
Reflect on the nature of necessary knowledge
Consider why knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness becomes necessary (daruri) through miracles and tawatur. This distinguishes it from theoretical reasoning.
This connects to broader themes in kalam about certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على أنْ أكذب على الملكِ بمرأى منهُ ومَسْمَعِ ، مع علمي بعظيم سطوتِهِ وقهرِهِ ، وأليم عقوبتِهِ لَمَنْ تَعَرَّضَ لجنابِهِ العلي واستخف بعظيم أمرِه ؟! فأي سماء تظلُّني ، وأي أرض تقلُّني .. إن كذبتُ عنه حرفاً ؟! وأنا أتحقَّقُ أني لو تقوَّلْتُ عليهِ بعض الأقاويل ، وفُهْتُ لكم عنهُ خُلْفاً . . لأخذ مني باليمين ، ولقطع مني الوتين ، ولا أجد منكم أحداً عنِّي حاجزين .
ثم إن لم يقنعكم هذا في تحققِ صِدْقِ مقالتي ، واستربتُم فيَّ معَ ما جرَّبْتُمُ التجريب التام مِنْ كمال نصحي لكم ، وشدَّةِ رأفتي بكم ، وعظيم شفقتي ، وشَرَفِ سابقتي ، وتنزهي عن كل رذيلة ، خصوصاً رذيلة الكذب وما تتحققونَ مِنْ حُسْنِ سيرتي.. فهنا ما يقطعُ العذر لكلِّ أحدٍ ، وتطلعُ به شموس المعرفة الضرورية على آفاقِ القلوب حتى لا ينكرها إلا مَنْ تعرَّضَ لسخط الملكِ وحقَّتْ عليه كلمةُ العذابِ فعاندَ وجَحَدَ ؛ وذلكَ أَنْ أَسأَلَ الملك كما تفضَّلَ ببعثي إليكم لبيان مراشدكم وإنذاركم قبل هجوم ما يفوتُ معَهُ استعدادكم لمعادِكم.. يتفضَّلُ أيضاً بإبانة صدقي فيما عنهُ بلَّغْتُ ، وأنّي ما كذبتُ عنه وما نَزَغْتُ ؛ بأنْ يخرقَ عادتَهُ ، ويفعل كذا وكذا ممَّا ليسَ عادته أن يفعله ويخصني بالإجابة بذلك المصدِّقِ الفارقِ ، دونَ مَنْ يقومُ منكم يسأله مثل ذلكَ الخارقِ يبتغي به معارضتي ، وتكذيبي في مقالتي ؛ إذْ ليس هو في الصِّدْقِ على مثل حالتي
ثم قالَ : أَيُّها الملكُ ؛ إنْ كنتُ صادقاً فيما بلَّغْتُ عنك . . فاخرق عادتكَ ، وافعل كذا
فأجابَهُ الملكُ إلى ذلكَ ، وفعلَهُ على وَفْقِ ما سألَ
وقد علم الجميعُ أَنَّهُ لا يُتوصَّل إلى مثل ذلكَ الفعلِ مِنَ الملك بحيلةٍ مِنَ الحيل
فلا خفاءَ أَنَّ ذلكَ الفعلَ مِنَ الملكِ يتنزَّلُ منزلةَ تصريحِهِ بصِدْقِ الشخص في كلِّ ما يُبلغ عنه ، والعلم بذلك ضروري لمَنْ حضرَ ذلكَ المجلس أو غابَ عنهُ ووصله خبره بالتواتر .
ولا يخفى : أنَّ هذا المثالَ مطابق لحالِ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام ، ولا خفاءَ أَنَّهُ قد عُلِمَ ضرورةً مِنْ سيرتهم عليهم الصلاة السلامُ التزامُ الصِّدْقِ ، ورفع الهمَّةِ عن كل دناءة ، والزهد في الدنيا بأسرها ؛ بحيث استوى عندهم ذهبها ومدرُها ، والتزام غـايـة التـواضـع مـع الفقراء والمساكين ، وإسقاط الجاه والمنزلة عندَ الخَلْقِ ، وطلبها
Such that I would lie against the king within his sight and hearing, while knowing his great power and his overwhelming might and the painful punishment for anyone who shows disrespect to his lofty station and makes light of his great command?! Then which sky would shade me, and which earth would carry me… if I lied about him in a single letter? And I am certain that if I fabricated sayings against him and spoke to you differently from him, he would seize me by the right hand, and cut my aorta, and you would find none among you to shield me. Then if this does not convince you of the truth of my statement, and you are suspicious of me despite your thorough experience of the perfection of my counsel to you, the intensity of my compassion for you, my great mercy, the honor of my precedence, my purity from every vice, especially the vice of lying, and your verification of the goodness of my conduct—then here is something that cuts off every excuse, and by it the suns of necessary knowledge rise upon the horizons of hearts so that none denies it except one who incurs the king's wrath and the word of punishment becomes due upon him, so he obstinately persists and denies. That is: I ask the king—just as He has graciously sent me to you to guide you and warn you before the sudden arrival of that which with your preparedness for your return becomes useless—He also graciously shows my truthfulness in what I have conveyed from Him, and that I have not lied about Him nor deviated, by breaking His custom and doing such-and-such which is not His custom to do, and He singles me out with that distinguishing confirmation, apart from anyone among you who asks Him for a similar miracle seeking to oppose me and deny my statement, for he is not in the same truthful condition as I am. Then he said: O king, if I am truthful in what I have conveyed from you, then break your custom and do such-and-such. So the king granted him that and did it according to what he asked. And everyone knew that it is not possible to achieve such an act from the king by any stratagem. So it is clear that that act from the king takes the place of his explicit declaration of the truthfulness of the person in everything he conveys about him, and the knowledge of that is necessary for whoever attended that assembly or was absent and the news reached him via successive transmission (tawatur). And it is not hidden that this example applies to the condition of the messengers (upon them peace and blessings). And it is not hidden that it is known necessarily from their conduct (upon them peace and blessings) their adherence to truthfulness, raising of aspiration above every baseness, asceticism in this entire world so that its gold and its dust are equal in their eyes, and their adherence to utmost humility with the poor and needy, and relinquishing status and position among people, and seeking it not.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof for the truthfulness of prophets, presented through an analogy. The author imagines a messenger sent by a king to convey a message. The messenger argues that it would be unthinkable for him to lie about the king, given the king's power and severe punishment. He then proposes a test: he will ask the king to perform an extraordinary act (breaking his custom) that only the king can do, to confirm his truthfulness. The king does so, and everyone universally knows that this act is an undeniable confirmation of the messenger's honesty. This knowledge is necessary for those who witness it or receive it via tawatur. The author then explicitly states that this example perfectly applies to the prophets: their miracles serve as divine confirmations, and their lives demonstrate truthfulness, asceticism, and humility. The proof establishes that miracles are God's authentication of a prophet's claim, making belief in their truthfulness necessary.

Key Terms
رسل
صدق
معجزة
خرق عادة
ضروري
تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the miracle itself is the proof, independent of the prophet's request and character.
Correction: This passage shows the miracle is a divine response to the prophet's request, analogous to a king confirming his messenger, and the prophet's character also supports his truthfulness.

Checkpoint
In the analogy, what does the king's extraordinary act (miracle) demonstrate?
A) The king's power
B) The messenger's truthfulness
C) The king's mercy
D) The messenger's courage

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine confirmations of prophetic truthfulness, and belief in them is necessary for anyone who learns of them through authentic transmission (tawatur).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The messenger relied on his known character of truthfulness. If your life were scrutinized, would your honesty and integrity testify to the truth you claim to believe? What would need to change?
?
The miracle cuts off all excuses. Are you harboring any excuse or doubt that keeps you from fully submitting to the Prophet's message? What would it take for you to accept that the signs are sufficient?
?
You have heard of the Prophet's miracles through tawatur. Do you possess necessary knowledge that he is truthful, or is your belief merely academic? How would your daily actions differ if you truly internalized that God authenticated him?

Prophethood
intermediate

The King's Analogy and Moral Perfection as Proofs of Prophethood
Sanusi argues for prophetic truthfulness via miracle analogy and moral perfection known by tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses a king's compliance with a miracle request and the widely known moral perfection of the prophets to prove their truthfulness.

Core Idea
Two independent proofs—miracle analogy and tawatur of character—establish prophetic truthfulness.

Sanusi presents a vivid analogy: a person asks a king to break his habit by performing a miracle, and the king's compliance proves the person's truthfulness. He then argues that the prophets' known moral excellence, transmitted widely, provides an independent proof. This lesson unpacks this twofold argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the king analogy
Read how a king's unusual act serves as a sign of truthfulness for the messenger. Notice that this knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī) for witnesses or those who receive the report via tawatur.
The analogy is concrete and logical.
2
See the analogy applied to prophets
Sanusi explicitly states that this example matches the situation of the messengers (peace be upon them). Reflect on how miracles function as divine confirmations.
3
Examine the prophets' moral qualities from tawatur
Identify the list of moral traits Sanusi mentions: truthfulness, renunciation, humility, compassion, sincerity, fear of God, perseverance, equality in calling, and endurance of harm.
These qualities are known necessarily from their biographies.
4
Grasp why moral perfection is a separate proof
Sanusi argues that such perfection cannot be feigned; only one truly on the truth would endure such hardship without worldly gain. This complements the miracle evidence.
5
Recognize the cumulative conclusion
Together, the miracle analogy and the tawatur of moral character provide airtight proof that the prophets are truthful in what they convey from Allah.
Both lines of evidence are necessary for a complete argument.

عادته أن يفعله ويخصني بالإجابة بذلك المصدِّقِ الفارقِ، دونَ مَنْ يقومُ منكم يسأله مثل ذلكَ الخارقِ يبتغي به معارضتي، وتكذيبي في مقالتي؛ إذْ ليس هو في الصِّدْقِ على مثل حالتي. ثم قالَ: أَيُّها الملكُ؛ إنْ كنتُ صادقاً فيما بلَّغْتُ عنك . . فاخرق عادتكَ، وافعل كذا. فأجابَهُ الملكُ إلى ذلكَ، وفعلَهُ على وَفْقِ ما سألَ. وقد علم الجميعُ أَنَّهُ لا يُتوصَّل إلى مثل ذلكَ الفعلِ مِنَ الملك بحيلةٍ مِنَ الحيل. فلا خفاءَ أَنَّ ذلكَ الفعلَ مِنَ الملكِ يتنزَّلُ منزلةَ تصريحِهِ بصِدْقِ الشخص في كلِّ ما يُبلغ عنه، والعلم بذلك ضروري لمَنْ حضرَ ذلكَ المجلس أو غابَ عنهُ ووصله خبره بالتواتر. ولا يخفى: أنَّ هذا المثالَ مطابق لحالِ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلام، ولا خفاءَ أَنَّهُ قد عُلِمَ ضرورةً مِنْ سيرتهم عليهم الصلاة السلامُ التزامُ الصِّدْقِ، ورفع الهمَّةِ عن كل دناءة، والزهد في الدنيا بأسرها؛ بحيث استوى عندهم ذهبها ومدرُها، والتزام غـايـة التـواضـع مـع الفقراء والمساكين، وإسقاط الجاه والمنزلة عندَ الخَلْقِ، وطلبها عند الملكِ الحقِّ، وعظيم ما جُبلوا عليهِ مِنَ الشفقة على المخلوقين، والنصحُ التام لعبادِ اللهِ تعالى، وكثرةُ جميع الخوف منه جل وعزَّ، والمبادرة لامتثالِ ما بَلَّغوا عنه قبل كلَّ أحدٍ، والمواظبة إلى المماتِ على دعاءِ الخَلْقِ إِلى اللهِ تعالى، مع التسوية في ذلك بين وضيعهم ورفيعهم، وغنيّهم وفقيرهم، وفطينهم وبليـدهـم، وأعجمهم وفصيحهم، وحُرِّهم وعبدهم، وذكرهم وأنثاهم، وحاضرهم وغائبهم، وملكهم وسوقتِهم. ثم سعةُ الصدورِ لحمْلِ سوء إيذائهم وشدَّةِ جفائهم والرأفة على جميعهم أكثرَ مِنْ رأفتهم على أولادهم بل وعلى أنفسهم، مِنْ غيرِ عوض يأخذونه منهم، ولا منفعة دنيوية تحصل لهم مِنْ قِبَلِهم، بل هم عليهم الصلاة والسلام تعرَّضوا بذلك لشدائد وأهوال نالَتْهم مِنْ جهتِهم، لا يثبتُ إلا مَنْ هو على صميمِ الحقِّ، قد شغلَهُ التلذذ برضا مولاه، عن أن يستعظم شيئاً يوصله إلى مراده منه ومناه. وقد ثبت بالتواتر ما نالهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ مِنْ عظيم إذايةِ الخلْقِ بسببِ دعائهم إلى اللهِ تعالى، حتى إنَّهم تجاسروا على أفضل الخلْقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فَآذَوهُ، وضيقوا عليه
His habit was to do it, and he singles me out for a response with that distinguishing sign of truthfulness, unlike anyone among you who asks him for such a miracle, seeking thereby to oppose me and deny my claim; since he is not in truthfulness like my state. Then he said: O king, if I am truthful in what I have conveyed from you... then break your habit and do such-and-such. So the king responded to that and did it in accordance with what he asked. And everyone knew that such an act from the king cannot be attained by any stratagem. So there is no doubt that that act from the king takes the place of his explicit declaration of the person's truthfulness in everything he conveys about him, and knowledge of that is necessary for one who attended that assembly or was absent from it and to whom the report reached via recurrent transmission. And it is not hidden that this example matches the situation of the messengers, peace be upon them. And there is no doubt that it is necessarily known from their biographies, peace be upon them, that they adhered to truthfulness, raised their aspiration above every baseness, and renounced this world entirely, such that gold and clay were equal to them; and they adhered to utmost humility with the poor and needy, and abandoned status and rank before creation, and sought it before the True King; and the great compassion with which they were endowed for creatures, and complete sincerity to the servants of Allah Almighty, and abundance of fear of Him, may He be glorified and exalted, and their haste to comply with what they conveyed about Him before everyone, and their perseverance until death in calling creation to Allah Almighty, with equality in that between their lowly and their noble, their rich and their poor, their intelligent and their dull, their non-Arab and their eloquent, their free and their slave, their male and their female, their present and their absent, their king and their marketplace folk. Then, breadth of heart to bear the evil of their harm and the severity of their harshness, and compassion for all of them more than their compassion for their own children, even for themselves, without any compensation they take from them, nor any worldly benefit accruing to them from them; rather they, peace be upon them, exposed themselves thereby to severe hardships and terrors that befell them from their direction, which none endures except one who is on the solid core of truth, whom delight in the pleasure of his Lord has occupied so that he does not consider great anything that brings him to his goal and wish. And it has been established by recurrent transmission what befell them, peace be upon them, of great harm from creation due to their calling to Allah Almighty, until they dared against the best of creation and the most honorable of them to Allah, our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and they harmed him and made things difficult for him.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a proof of prophetic truthfulness using a concrete analogy together with evidence from the prophets' moral character known by tawatur (recurrent transmission). The author first narrates an example: a person asks a king to break his habit by performing an unusual act as a sign that the person is truthful in what he conveys from the king. The king complies, and everyone understands that this act is equivalent to an explicit declaration of the person's truthfulness. This knowledge is necessary (ḍarūrī) for witnesses or for those who receive the report via tawatur. The author then states that this example matches the situation of the messengers (peace be upon them). He asserts that it is necessarily known from their biographies that they adhered to truthfulness (ṣidq), elevated aspiration (himma) above any baseness, and renounced worldly goods. They showed utmost humility, compassion, sincerity, fear of God, haste to obey, perseverance in calling people to God with complete equality regardless of social status, and endurance of harm and hardship without seeking worldly compensation. Such perfection cannot be simulated except by one who is truly on the truth. Finally, the author notes that the harm they endured is also established by tawatur, even the harm inflicted upon the best of creation, Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). This cumulative evidence—miracles (khawāriq) and moral perfection known by tawatur—logically entails the truthfulness of the prophets.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof of prophethood relies only on miracles.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the prophets' known moral perfection (by tawatur) is equally essential and provides a separate, complementary argument.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the role of the prophets' character traits known by tawatur in proving their truthfulness?
A) They are irrelevant; only miracles matter.
B) They weaken the proof because they show worldly motives.
C) They provide independent evidence that reinforces the miracle argument.
D) They are only known by personal opinion, not reliable.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's proof for prophetic truthfulness combines the miracle-based analogy with the widely known moral perfection of the prophets, both established by tawatur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are faced with a situation where telling the truth will cost you your reputation, comfort, or relationships, do you cling to truthfulness like the prophets or do you compromise for worldly gain? What is one step you will take today to prioritize truth over ease?
?
The prophets endured severe harm and hardship while calling people to Allah, without seeking any worldly return. What harm or inconvenience have you suffered recently for the sake of your faith? If none, are you actively striving in a way that would require such sacrifice?
?
The prophets showed perfect equality between rich and poor, noble and lowly, friend and enemy. Is there someone you treat differently based on their status or background? How can you begin to treat all people with the same compassion and sincerity as the prophets did?

Prophethood

The Prophets' Character and Suffering as Proof
Sanusi enumerates prophetic virtues and their suffering as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the prophets' impeccable character and their patient endurance of harm without worldly gain constitute a compelling circumstantial evidence (qarīna ḥāliyya) of their truthfulness.

Core Idea
The prophets' conduct and suffering alone prove their sincerity.

In this passage, Sanusi builds a multi-layered argument for the truthfulness of the prophets. He begins by detailing their innate qualities—compassion, sincerity, fear of Allah, and dedication to calling people to Allah with equality. He then contrasts this with the severe harm they endured from their people, especially the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ). By examining their perfect character alongside their patient suffering, Sanusi argues that such a combination is a clear sign that they could not be liars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Source Passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Pay attention to the long list of virtues and the description of the Prophet's suffering.
Note the shift from describing virtues to describing harm endured.
2
Identify the Two Key Evidences
Find the two main parts: (1) the prophets' innate qualities and conduct, (2) the persecution they faced. Understand how each part supports their truthfulness.
The author calls the combination a circumstantial evidence.
3
Reflect on the Rhetorical Question
Consider the rhetorical question about the face of the Prophet being bloodied. How does this strengthen the argument?
It emphasizes the injustice and the Prophet's mercy.

عند الملكِ الحقِّ ، وعظيم ما جُبلوا عليهِ مِنَ الشفقة على المخلوقين ، والنصحُ التام لعبادِ اللهِ تعالى ، وكثرةُ جميع الخوف منه جل وعزَّ ، والمبادرة لامتثالِ ما بَلَّغوا عنه قبل كلَّ أحدٍ ، والمواظبة إلى المماتِ على دعاءِ الخَلْقِ إِلى اللهِ تعالى ، مع التسوية في ذلك بين وضيعهم ورفيعهم ، وغنيّهم وفقيرهم ، وفطينهم وبليـدهـم ، وأعجمهم وفصيحهم، وحُرِّهم وعبدهم، وذكرهم وأنثاهم ، وحاضرهم وغائبهم ، وملكهم وسوقتِهم . ثم سعةُ الصدورِ لحمْلِ سوء إيذائهم وشدَّةِ جفائهم والرأفة على جميعهم أكثرَ مِنْ رأفتهم على أولادهم بل وعلى أنفسهم ، مِنْ غيرِ عوض يأخذونه منهم ، ولا منفعة دنيوية تحصل لهم مِنْ قِبَلِهم ، بل هم عليهم الصلاة والسلام تعرَّضوا بذلك لشدائد وأهوال نالَتْهم مِنْ جهتِهم ، لا يثبتُ إلا مَنْ هو على صميمِ الحقِّ ، قد شغلَهُ التلذذ برضا مولاه ، عن أن يستعظم شيئاً يوصله إلى مراده منه ومناه لها . وقد ثبت بالتواتر ما نالهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ مِنْ عظيم إذايةِ الخلْقِ بسببِ دعائهم إلى اللهِ تعالى ، حتى إنَّهم تجاسروا على أفضل الخلْقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فَآذَوهُ ، وضيقوا عليهِ وقاتلوه ، حتى إنَّهم كسروا رَباعِيَتَهُ ، وأَدْمَوا منه ذلكَ الوجْهَ الأبهى الأرفع الكريم ، وحُجبوا لشقائهم عن مشاهدة تلك المحاسن التي الكشفُ عن أدناها يَذْهَشُ الفكر ، ويُسْكِرُ النفس ؛ بما ترى مِنْ خَرْقِ العادةِ في ذلكَ الخَلْقِ الوسيمِ والخُلُقِ العظيم . وكيف يفلح قومٌ أدْمَوا وجْهَ نبيهم الرؤوف عليهم وقدِ استقبلهم بشموس طلعته ، ومحاسن قمر وجهه ، مُباشراً لهم بتلك الذاتِ الزكيَّةِ المرفّعةِ ؛ ليأخذ بحُجَزِهم عنِ النار ، حريصاً على ردّهم عنها ولو بالسيف قبل أن يفوتهم ؟! الأمرُ بالحلول في دارِ البوارِ . فهذا كلُّه يدلُّ بمُجرَّدِهِ على أنَّهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام صادقون في كلِّ ما أَتَوا بهِ عن الله تعالى ، وقرينة حالهم وحدها تنافي حالة الكذب ضرورة . كيف وقد أَيَّدَهمُ الله تعالى بخوارقَ يُقطَعُ بأَنَّهُ لا يُتوصل إليها بحيلة سحر ولا غوص في طب ولا غيره ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وفلْقِ البحرِ أطواداً ، ونحو ذلكَ ممَّا لا يُتوصَّلُ إليه بالحِيَلِ ؛ إذ لو كانَ يُتوصَّلُ إليه بالحِيَل لاستحال عادةً أن ينفردوا بذلك عن جميع أهل الأرض ؟! هذا ؛ وقد عُلِمَ ضرورةً أنَّهم كانوا في غاية البعد عن
Before the True King, and the great innate disposition upon them of compassion for created beings, and perfect sincerity for the servants of Allah the Exalted, and the abundance of all fear of Him, may He be glorified and exalted, and hastening to obey what they conveyed from Him before anyone, and perseverance until death in calling creation to Allah the Exalted, with equality in that between their lowly and their high, their rich and their poor, their intelligent and their stupid, their non-Arab and their eloquent, their free and their slave, their male and their female, their present and their absent, their king and their commoner. Then, broadness of chest for bearing the evil of their harm and the severity of their harshness, and compassion for all of them more than their compassion for their own children, indeed more than for themselves, without any compensation they take from them, nor any worldly benefit that comes to them from them. Rather, they (peace and blessings be upon them) exposed themselves thereby to hardships and terrors that befell them from their direction; none remains firm except one who is on the essence of truth, whom the delight of his Lord's pleasure occupies from considering great any thing that brings him to his desire and wish for it. And it has been established by tawātur (mass transmission) what befell them (peace and blessings be upon them) of great harm from creation due to their calling to Allah the Exalted, such that they dared against the best of creation and the most noble of them before Allah the Exalted, our Prophet and our Master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), so they harmed him, and constrained him, and fought him, until indeed they broke his incisor tooth, and made bleed from him that most radiant, most exalted, and noble face, and they were veiled by their wretchedness from witnessing those beauties, the disclosure of the least of which bewilders the mind and intoxicates the soul; as you see of breaking of custom in that handsome form and great character. And how can a people succeed who made bleed the face of their merciful prophet, while he faced them with the suns of his countenance and the beauties of the moon of his face, directly meeting them with that pure, elevated essence, to take them by their garments from the Fire, eager to turn them away from it even with the sword before they miss it? The matter leads to dwelling in the abode of perdition. So all this by itself indicates that they (peace and blessings be upon them) are truthful in everything they brought from Allah the Exalted, and the circumstantial evidence of their state alone contradicts the state of lying necessarily. How could it be, when Allah the Exalted supported them with miraculous wonders (kharq al-ʿādāt) about which it is decisively known that they cannot be attained by trickery of magic nor delving into medicine nor other than that; such as reviving the dead, splitting the sea into mountains, and the like of that which cannot be attained by tricks. For if they could be attained by tricks, it would be impossible by custom that they alone would be distinguished in that from all the people of the earth. This; and it is known necessarily that they were in the utmost distance from
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the truthfulness of the prophets (peace be upon them). The author, Sanusi, presents a multi-layered argument. First, he describes the prophets' innate qualities: their compassion, sincerity, fear of Allah, diligence in conveying the message, and complete equality in calling everyone to Allah. Then he notes their extraordinary patience—bearing immense harm for the sake of the call, without seeking worldly reward. He argues that such steadfastness can only come from one deeply rooted in truth and absorbed in the pleasure of his Lord. Second, he cites the historical fact (established by tawatur) of the severe persecution they endured, especially the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), who was physically attacked and wounded. Sanusi uses a rhetorical question to emphasize the impossibility that people could harm a merciful prophet and still succeed; the very act of wounding such a noble figure indicates their wretchedness. Third, he concludes that the entire situation—the prophets' impeccable conduct and the harm they faced—constitutes a circumstantial evidence (qarīna ḥāliyya) that necessarily excludes the possibility of their lying. To strengthen the argument, he adds the evidence of miracles (khawāriq al-ʿādāt), which are beyond human capability and serve as divine confirmation. He notes that miracles like reviving the dead and splitting the sea are so extraordinary that if they could be produced by tricks, the prophets would not be unique in performing them. Thus, the combination of their character, their suffering, and their miracles provides a decisive proof of their truthfulness.

Key Terms
قرينة حال (qarīna ḥāliyya)
التواتر (tawātur)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prophets' suffering alone is insufficient proof of their truthfulness.
Correction: Sanusi argues that the combination of their perfect character and patient suffering without worldly gain constitutes a strong circumstantial evidence that necessarily excludes falsehood, especially when supported by tawātur transmission of the events.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi mean by 'قرينة حالهم وحدها تنافي حالة الكذب ضرورة'?
A) The prophets' state indicates they were poor
B) Their state alone necessarily points to truthfulness
C) They were forced to lie
D) Their miracles prove everything

Key Takeaway
The prophets' exemplary character and their selfless endurance of persecution together form a powerful circumstantial evidence that they were truthful in their message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face rejection or harm for your faith, do you feel a sense of entitlement to reward from people, or can you truly say you expect nothing from them? What does your reaction reveal about the depth of your sincerity before Allah?
?
If you were to be mistreated by someone you are trying to guide, would you continue to show them compassion more than you show your own family? What holds you back from that prophetic standard?
?
The Prophet's face was bloodied and his tooth broken while he was trying to save people from the Fire. Have you ever felt that your efforts to guide others cost you something precious? Are you willing to pay that price without expecting any return? What would it take for you to reach that level of selflessness?

Miracles as Divine Confirmation of Prophethood
Sanusi adds miracles as a further proof of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that miracles (khawāriq al-ʿādāt) serve as an additional, decisive proof of the prophets' truthfulness because they are beyond any human trick or natural cause.

Core Idea
Miracles are divine acts that confirm the prophets' truth beyond any doubt.

After establishing the circumstantial evidence from the prophets' character and suffering, Sanusi adds a second layer of proof: miracles. He argues that the prophets were supported by extraordinary events that cannot be produced by magic, medicine, or any trick. The uniqueness of these miracles—such as reviving the dead and splitting the sea—shows they are from Allah and therefore confirm the truth of the prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the Source Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the transition from the previous argument to the discussion of miracles.
The phrase 'كيف وقد أَيَّدَهمُ الله تعالى' marks the shift.
2
Understand the Nature of Miracles
Identify how Sanusi describes miracles: as 'خوارق العادات' (breaks in custom) that cannot be achieved by tricks. Note the examples given.
Miracles are beyond human capability.
3
Analyze the Argument for Uniqueness
Consider the reasoning: if miracles could be produced by tricks, they would not be exclusive to the prophets. Why does this strengthen the proof?
Uniqueness indicates divine intervention.

عند الملكِ الحقِّ ، وعظيم ما جُبلوا عليهِ مِنَ الشفقة على المخلوقين ، والنصحُ التام لعبادِ اللهِ تعالى ، وكثرةُ جميع الخوف منه جل وعزَّ ، والمبادرة لامتثالِ ما بَلَّغوا عنه قبل كلَّ أحدٍ ، والمواظبة إلى المماتِ على دعاءِ الخَلْقِ إِلى اللهِ تعالى ، مع التسوية في ذلك بين وضيعهم ورفيعهم ، وغنيّهم وفقيرهم ، وفطينهم وبليـدهـم ، وأعجمهم وفصيحهم، وحُرِّهم وعبدهم، وذكرهم وأنثاهم ، وحاضرهم وغائبهم ، وملكهم وسوقتِهم . ثم سعةُ الصدورِ لحمْلِ سوء إيذائهم وشدَّةِ جفائهم والرأفة على جميعهم أكثرَ مِنْ رأفتهم على أولادهم بل وعلى أنفسهم ، مِنْ غيرِ عوض يأخذونه منهم ، ولا منفعة دنيوية تحصل لهم مِنْ قِبَلِهم ، بل هم عليهم الصلاة والسلام تعرَّضوا بذلك لشدائد وأهوال نالَتْهم مِنْ جهتِهم ، لا يثبتُ إلا مَنْ هو على صميمِ الحقِّ ، قد شغلَهُ التلذذ برضا مولاه ، عن أن يستعظم شيئاً يوصله إلى مراده منه ومناه لها . وقد ثبت بالتواتر ما نالهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ مِنْ عظيم إذايةِ الخلْقِ بسببِ دعائهم إلى اللهِ تعالى ، حتى إنَّهم تجاسروا على أفضل الخلْقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فَآذَوهُ ، وضيقوا عليهِ وقاتلوه ، حتى إنَّهم كسروا رَباعِيَتَهُ ، وأَدْمَوا منه ذلكَ الوجْهَ الأبهى الأرفع الكريم ، وحُجبوا لشقائهم عن مشاهدة تلك المحاسن التي الكشفُ عن أدناها يَذْهَشُ الفكر ، ويُسْكِرُ النفس ؛ بما ترى مِنْ خَرْقِ العادةِ في ذلكَ الخَلْقِ الوسيمِ والخُلُقِ العظيم . وكيف يفلح قومٌ أدْمَوا وجْهَ نبيهم الرؤوف عليهم وقدِ استقبلهم بشموس طلعته ، ومحاسن قمر وجهه ، مُباشراً لهم بتلك الذاتِ الزكيَّةِ المرفّعةِ ؛ ليأخذ بحُجَزِهم عنِ النار ، حريصاً على ردّهم عنها ولو بالسيف قبل أن يفوتهم ؟! الأمرُ بالحلول في دارِ البوارِ . فهذا كلُّه يدلُّ بمُجرَّدِهِ على أنَّهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام صادقون في كلِّ ما أَتَوا بهِ عن الله تعالى ، وقرينة حالهم وحدها تنافي حالة الكذب ضرورة . كيف وقد أَيَّدَهمُ الله تعالى بخوارقَ يُقطَعُ بأَنَّهُ لا يُتوصل إليها بحيلة سحر ولا غوص في طب ولا غيره ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وفلْقِ البحرِ أطواداً ، ونحو ذلكَ ممَّا لا يُتوصَّلُ إليه بالحِيَلِ ؛ إذ لو كانَ يُتوصَّلُ إليه بالحِيَل لاستحال عادةً أن ينفردوا بذلك عن جميع أهل الأرض ؟! هذا ؛ وقد عُلِمَ ضرورةً أنَّهم كانوا في غاية البعد عن
Before the True King, and the great innate disposition upon them of compassion for created beings, and perfect sincerity for the servants of Allah the Exalted, and the abundance of all fear of Him, may He be glorified and exalted, and hastening to obey what they conveyed from Him before anyone, and perseverance until death in calling creation to Allah the Exalted, with equality in that between their lowly and their high, their rich and their poor, their intelligent and their stupid, their non-Arab and their eloquent, their free and their slave, their male and their female, their present and their absent, their king and their commoner. Then, broadness of chest for bearing the evil of their harm and the severity of their harshness, and compassion for all of them more than their compassion for their own children, indeed more than for themselves, without any compensation they take from them, nor any worldly benefit that comes to them from them. Rather, they (peace and blessings be upon them) exposed themselves thereby to hardships and terrors that befell them from their direction; none remains firm except one who is on the essence of truth, whom the delight of his Lord's pleasure occupies from considering great any thing that brings him to his desire and wish for it. And it has been established by tawātur (mass transmission) what befell them (peace and blessings be upon them) of great harm from creation due to their calling to Allah the Exalted, such that they dared against the best of creation and the most noble of them before Allah the Exalted, our Prophet and our Master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), so they harmed him, and constrained him, and fought him, until indeed they broke his incisor tooth, and made bleed from him that most radiant, most exalted, and noble face, and they were veiled by their wretchedness from witnessing those beauties, the disclosure of the least of which bewilders the mind and intoxicates the soul; as you see of breaking of custom in that handsome form and great character. And how can a people succeed who made bleed the face of their merciful prophet, while he faced them with the suns of his countenance and the beauties of the moon of his face, directly meeting them with that pure, elevated essence, to take them by their garments from the Fire, eager to turn them away from it even with the sword before they miss it? The matter leads to dwelling in the abode of perdition. So all this by itself indicates that they (peace and blessings be upon them) are truthful in everything they brought from Allah the Exalted, and the circumstantial evidence of their state alone contradicts the state of lying necessarily. How could it be, when Allah the Exalted supported them with miraculous wonders (kharq al-ʿādāt) about which it is decisively known that they cannot be attained by trickery of magic nor delving into medicine nor other than that; such as reviving the dead, splitting the sea into mountains, and the like of that which cannot be attained by tricks. For if they could be attained by tricks, it would be impossible by custom that they alone would be distinguished in that from all the people of the earth. This; and it is known necessarily that they were in the utmost distance from
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a proof of the truthfulness of the prophets (peace be upon them). The author, Sanusi, presents a multi-layered argument. First, he describes the prophets' innate qualities: their compassion, sincerity, fear of Allah, diligence in conveying the message, and complete equality in calling everyone to Allah. Then he notes their extraordinary patience—bearing immense harm for the sake of the call, without seeking worldly reward. He argues that such steadfastness can only come from one deeply rooted in truth and absorbed in the pleasure of his Lord. Second, he cites the historical fact (established by tawatur) of the severe persecution they endured, especially the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), who was physically attacked and wounded. Sanusi uses a rhetorical question to emphasize the impossibility that people could harm a merciful prophet and still succeed; the very act of wounding such a noble figure indicates their wretchedness. Third, he concludes that the entire situation—the prophets' impeccable conduct and the harm they faced—constitutes a circumstantial evidence (qarīna ḥāliyya) that necessarily excludes the possibility of their lying. To strengthen the argument, he adds the evidence of miracles (khawāriq al-ʿādāt), which are beyond human capability and serve as divine confirmation. He notes that miracles like reviving the dead and splitting the sea are so extraordinary that if they could be produced by tricks, the prophets would not be unique in performing them. Thus, the combination of their character, their suffering, and their miracles provides a decisive proof of their truthfulness.

Key Terms
خوارق العادات (khawāriq al-ʿādāt)
نبينا ومولانا محمد (our Prophet and Master Muhammad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are just advanced magic or tricks that anyone can learn.
Correction: Sanusi argues that miracles are decisively beyond any trick, magic, or natural science. Their uniqueness to prophets shows they are divine acts, not human feats.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, why can miracles not be attributed to tricks?
A) The prophets were experts in magic
B) They are too many to count
C) If tricks could produce them, others would also perform them
D) The miracles have no witnesses

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine acts that, because of their uniqueness and impossibility by human means, confirm the truthfulness of the prophets beyond any doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that the prophets' miracles are decisive proofs from Allah, why do you still hesitate to fully submit to His commands in areas where you have no direct miracle? What is keeping you from trusting His Word as if you saw the sea split before your eyes?
?
When you read about the reviving of the dead or the splitting of the sea, do you feel a sense of awe that leads to action, or do you treat these as distant stories? Which miracle do you most struggle to internalize as real, and how would your life change if you were to live by its certainty?
?
Sanusi argues that miracles are beyond any human trick. Examine your own life: have you ever rationalized away a clear sign from Allah—either in creation or in your own experiences—because it required too much of you? What would it mean for you today to accept that no human trick can produce such signs, and to respond with full submission?
