Merciful Conduct as Proof of Prophetic Truthfulness
Author argues that prophets' merciful conduct despite harm proves their truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophets' gracious and merciful behavior, even when they are severely harmed, serves as a logical proof of their truthfulness in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
A prophet's character itself is a proof of his truthfulness.

This passage from the classical kalam text presents a unique argument for prophethood: not only miracles, but the prophet's own conduct—especially his mercy towards those who harm him—serves as powerful circumstantial evidence (قرينة حال) that he is truthful. By reflecting on the Prophet Muhammad's response to persecution, we see that such behavior is rationally incompatible with falsehood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the vivid description of the Prophet's injuries and his compassionate response.
The language is emotionally charged; the author intends to move the reader.
2
Identify the two key elements
Identify the harm inflicted on the Prophet (broken tooth, bleeding face) and his merciful reaction (facing them with his countenance, eager to save them from Hell).
3
Understand the logical conclusion
Reflect on the author's claim that this conduct alone (its mere existence) indicates truthfulness and necessarily repudiates falsehood. Ask yourself: why would a liar behave this way?
The argument is that such extraordinary mercy cannot coexist with deceit—it's a circumstantial proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقاتلوه ، حتى إنَّهم كسروا رَباعِيَتَهُ ، وأَدْمَوا منه ذلكَ الوجْهَ الأبهى الأرفع الكريم ، وحُجبوا لشقائهم عن مشاهدة تلك المحاسن التي الكشفُ عن أدناها يَذْهَشُ الفكر ، ويُسْكِرُ النفس ؛ بما ترى مِنْ خَرْقِ العادةِ في ذلكَ الخَلْقِ الوسيمِ والخُلُقِ العظيم . وكيف يفلح قومٌ أدْمَوا وجْهَ نبيهم الرؤوف عليهم وقدِ استقبلهم بشموس طلعته ، ومحاسن قمر وجهه ، مُباشراً لهم بتلك الذاتِ الزكيَّةِ المرفّعةِ ؛ ليأخذ بحُجَزِهم عنِ النار ، حريصاً على ردّهم عنها ولو بالسيف قبل أن يفوتهم ؟! الأمرُ بالحلول في دارِ البوارِ . فهذا كلُّه يدلُّ بمُجرَّدِهِ على أنَّهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام صادقون في كلِّ ما أَتَوا بهِ عن الله تعالى ، وقرينة حالهم وحدها تنافي حالة الكذب ضرورة .
And they fought him, to the point that they broke his incisor, and caused his radiant, exalted, noble face to bleed, and they were veiled, due to their misery, from observing those beauties the unveiling of the least of which baffles the mind and intoxicates the soul, by what you see of breaking of custom in that handsome form and great character. And how can a people prosper who caused the face of their compassionate prophet to bleed while he faced them with the suns of his countenance and the beauties of the moon of his face, directly confronting them with that pure, elevated essence, to seize them by their garments from the Fire, eager to turn them back from it even with the sword before they missed it? He was commanding to settle in the abode of perdition. All of this by itself indicates that they (peace and blessings be upon them) are truthful in everything they brought from Allah Almighty, and the evidence of their state alone necessarily repudiates the state of falsehood.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents an argument from the prophets' own character and conduct (especially their mercy towards those who harmed them) as a proof of their truthfulness. The author describes how the Prophet Muhammad was physically attacked yet remained compassionate, seeking to save his people. This extraordinary mercy, combined with their known moral excellence, is presented as a circumstantial evidence (قرينة حال) that itself precludes the possibility of them being liars. The author argues that such a demeanor is logically incompatible with deceit.

Key Terms
قرينة حال
صادقون
ضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that prophethood requires only miracles (mu'jizat) and that the prophet's personal conduct is irrelevant as evidence.
Correction: This passage shows that the prophet's own character and behavior — especially extraordinary mercy despite harm — is itself a form of evidence (قرينة حال) that proves truthfulness, independent of miracles.

Checkpoint
What does the author cite as evidence for the truthfulness of the prophets in this passage?
A) Their miracles
B) Their gracious conduct despite harm
C) Their being unlettered
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
The prophet's merciful conduct despite severe harm serves as a circumstantial proof (قرينة حال) that logically precludes the possibility of falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone hurts you deeply, do you find yourself responding with compassion or seeking revenge? How does the Prophet's response to having his incisor broken challenge your own reactions?
?
The author says the Prophet's conduct itself is proof of truthfulness. What does your own conduct in times of personal harm say about the truthfulness you claim to live by?
?
Can you identify a specific moment when you were wronged and your response either drew others closer to truth or pushed them away? What one concrete action can you take this week to mirror the Prophet's merciful response?

The Prophet's Illiteracy as Proof of Revelation
Author argues that the Prophet's known illiteracy and intense scrutiny by enemies prove he could not have forged the message.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's illiteracy and the intense scrutiny of his enemies prove that the Quran could not have been forged by him.

Core Idea
The Prophet's illiteracy turns weakness into the strongest proof.

This lesson presents a powerful argument from the Prophet's known illiteracy and the relentless investigation by his enemies. Both friends and foes admit he was unlettered, and yet despite their best efforts, no human source was ever found. This silence speaks volumes, confirming the divine origin of his message.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the use of Quranic evidence and the logical argument.
The passage combines revelation and rational reasoning.
2
Identify the two key premises
First, the Prophet's illiteracy is universally acknowledged. Second, his enemies had every motive to expose any human source but failed. Understand how these two facts work together.
The word 'العادة تحيل' indicates a rational judgement.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The only logical conclusion is that the Quran is from Allah. His illiteracy was not a weakness but a mark of its divine origin.
Consider how this rebuts the claim that the Prophet composed it himself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا ؛ وقد عُلِمَ ضرورةً أنَّهم كانوا في غاية البعد عن هذه العلوم وأربابها وأسبابها ، ﴿ وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُوا مِن قَبْلِهِ مِن كِتَبٍ وَلَا تَخُصُّهُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذَا لَأَرْتَابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ ﴾ [العنكبوت : ٤٨] ، وهذا ممَّا أقرَّ به الموافقُ والمخالفُ . هذا معَ أنَّ في نفوس الأعداء والحسدة ما يُحرِّكُ الدواعي إلى البحث والتفتيش ، والعادة تحيل أن تكون لهم نسبةً إلى شيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ إلا ويُعلَمُ ويُقرَّعونَ بهِ ، ويَشتي ويَسْتهِرُ أمره حتى لا يخفى على أحدٍ .
This; and it is known necessarily that they were in the utmost distance from these sciences, their masters, and their means. 'And you did not recite before it any book, nor did you inscribe it with your right hand; otherwise the falsifiers would have doubted' (al-Ankabut: 48). And this is something affirmed by both the opponent and the supporter. This, despite the fact that in the souls of enemies and jealous ones there is that which moves the motives to investigation and scrutiny, and custom deems it impossible that there would be any connection to any of that for them except that it would be known and they would be reproached with it, and it would spread and become notorious, until it is not hidden from anyone.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage adds another proof: the prophet's known illiteracy (being unlettered). The Quran itself challenges that he had no prior learning, and this is admitted by all. Moreover, given the intense scrutiny of enemies, if he had any human source, it would have been exposed. The fact that nothing was ever found despite their diligent search shows the divine origin.

Key Terms
الأُمِّي
العلوم
موافق ومخالف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's illiteracy makes him incapable of delivering the Quran, so it must be from someone else.
Correction: The author turns this around: his illiteracy proves he could not have composed it, so it must be from God.

Checkpoint
What role do the enemies play in this argument?
A) They confirm the miracles
B) They would have exposed any human source, but did not
C) They converted
D) They were powerless

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's illiteracy, combined with the failure of his enemies to find any human source, is a decisive proof for the divine origin of the Quran.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the enemies of the Prophet, with all their resources and motivation, could find no human source for the Quran, what does that say about your own doubts when they arise? Will you let this certainty from history silence every whisper of skepticism in your heart?
?
Imagine you had to defend the Quran's divine origin to a determined skeptic using only the argument in this passage. Would you be convinced? If not, what is holding you back from full conviction?
?
The fact that the Prophet was illiterate is not a weakness but the very proof of his prophethood. Is there an area in your life where you see your limitations as obstacles, rather than as opportunities for Allah's power to manifest? Will you trust Him today to turn your weakness into proof of His truth?

The Certainty of Prophetic Truthfulness and Infallibility
Author concludes on prophetic truthfulness, infallibility, and obligation to believe Prophet Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proofs for the truthfulness and infallibility of prophets, and why accepting the message of Prophet Muhammad is obligatory.

Core Idea
Prophets are truthful and sinless, proven by miracles and reason, making their message undeniable.

This passage from Sanusi's creed summarizes the key conclusions regarding the reliability of prophets. It establishes that their truthfulness is known necessarily, their infallibility from lying is proven rationally through miracles, and their sinlessness in general is derived from the fact that they are perfect role models. The author then highlights the unique status of Prophet Muhammad and the obligation to believe his teachings.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Absorb the author's summary style.
Notice the logical flow from general to specific.
2
Identify the three claims about prophets
The passage makes distinct claims: truthfulness is known necessarily, infallibility from lying is rational via miracles, and infallibility from sins is by consensus and logic. Locate each.
Track the different sources of knowledge: necessity, reason, consensus.
3
Reflect on the obligation to believe Prophet Muhammad
The author concludes that we must believe everything Prophet Muhammad brought, including bodily resurrection. Ask why this follows from the previous points.
Consider the role of miracles, especially the Quran, in confirming his truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فصِدْقُ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام معلوم على الضرورة لكل موفّق وعصمتُهم مِنَ الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة ، ومِنْ كبائر المعاصي وصغائرِ الخِسَّة بالإجماع ، ومِنْ سائرِ الذنوبِ ؛ فإنَّ الخَلْقَ المبعوثينَ هم إليهم مأمورون بالاقتداء بهم ، ولا يأمر تعالى بمعصية . وأفضلهم نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلَّمَ ، بعثَهُ الله سبحانَهُ إلى أهلِ الأَرضِ كافَّةً ، وأَيَّدَهُ بمعجزات لا حصر لها ، وأفضلها القرآن العظيم الذي إعجازه للخَلْقَ مُدْرَكُ بالعِيان إلى الآن فوجب تصديقه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في كل ما أتى به عن الله تعالى ؛ كالبعثِ لعين هذا البدنِ لا لمثلِهِ إجماعاً
In summary: The truthfulness of the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them) is known necessarily to every successful person, and their infallibility from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle, and from major sins and base minor sins by consensus, and from all other sins; for the creatures who are sent down are commanded to follow them, and Allah Almighty does not command disobedience. And the best of them is our Prophet, our master, our liege Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace). Allah sent him to all the people of the earth, and supported him with countless miracles, the best of which is the Great Qur'an, whose inimitability is perceived by the people until now. So it is obligatory to believe him (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) in everything he brought from Allah Almighty, such as the resurrection of the very same body, not a likeness, by consensus.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This is the concluding passage that summarizes the proofs for prophetic truthfulness and infallibility. The author states that the truthfulness of prophets is known necessarily (i.e., by immediate intuitive knowledge) to those who are guided. Their infallibility from lying is a rational conclusion based on miracles. Their infallibility from major sins and base minor sins is by consensus of the community, and from all sins because they are models to be followed and God would not command to follow a sinner. Then the author emphasizes the superiority of Prophet Muhammad, his universal mission, his countless miracles (especially the Quran which is perpetually miraculous), and the obligation to believe everything he brought, including the resurrection of the same body.

Key Terms
صدق
عصمة
ضرورة
إعجاز
بعث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are sinless because they are angels or have no human nature.
Correction: Infallibility means they are protected from error and sin, not that they lack human qualities; they remain perfect role models.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are prophets infallible from all sins?
A) Because they are angels
B) Because they are commanded to be followed and God does not command to follow a sinner
C) Because they are sinless by nature
D) Because they have no desires

Key Takeaway
The truthfulness and infallibility of prophets are proven by necessary knowledge, miracles, consensus, and the logic of role models, making their message binding upon all.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the truthfulness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is necessarily known to every successful person, then what does your hesitation in obeying some of his commands say about your own success? What is one command you struggle to implement wholeheartedly, and why do you resist it?
?
The Prophet (peace be upon him) is infallible from all sins because Allah would not send a sinner as a role model. In your daily life, do you actually treat him as the perfect role model, or do you pick and choose which parts of his example to follow? What area of your life have you refused to align with his sunnah?
?
The Qur'an is an enduring miracle that is perceptible to everyone until today. If you truly believed that, would your relationship with the Qur'an be the same? When was the last time it moved you to tears, action, or radical change? If it hasn't, what are you going to do about it starting today?

Prophethood

Truthfulness and Infallibility of Prophets
Sanusi states that prophethood is known necessarily and prophets are infallible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three aspects of prophetic infallibility and the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Prophets are truthful and sinless by necessity, miracle, consensus, and divine command.

Sanusi summarizes the necessary truthfulness of prophets and their complete infallibility. He distinguishes different types of sin and the evidence for each protection. This passage lays the foundation for understanding why prophets are trustworthy guides.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Sanusi structures his summary with 'wa' (and) to link each claim.
The passage is dense but logical.
2
Identify the three levels of infallibility
Find each level: (1) from lying by miracle, (2) from major and base minor sins by consensus, (3) from all other sins by reason.
Each level has a different kind of evidence: rational, consensus-based, and rational again.
3
Understand the reasoning for the third level
Ask yourself why prophets must be sinless in all other sins. Sanusi argues that because people are commanded to emulate prophets, and God does not command disobedience, prophets cannot commit any sin.
This connects prophethood to divine guidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فصدق الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام معلوم على الضرورة لكل موفّق وعصمتهم من الكذب معلومة عقلاً بدليل المعجزة ، ومن كبائر المعاصي وصغائر الخِسَّة بالإجماع ، ومن سائر الذنوب ؛ فإنَّ الخَلْقَ المبعوثينَ هم إليهم مأمورون بالاقتداء بهم ، ولا يأمر تعالى بمعصية .
In summary: the truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them, is known necessarily for every divinely guided person, and their infallibility from lying is known rationally by the evidence of the miracle, and from major sins and base minor sins by consensus, and from all other sins; for the people sent to them are commanded to emulate them, and God Most High does not command disobedience.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a summary statement on the truthfulness and infallibility of prophets. Sanusi begins by asserting that the truthfulness of the messengers is known necessarily (ḍarūra) to every person who is divinely guided (muwaffaq). This means it is a self-evident truth, not requiring elaborate proof. Then he explains their infallibility ('iṣma) in three levels: first, infallibility from lying is known rationally (ʿaqlan) by the evidence of the miracle (muʿjiza) — because the miracle is a divine confirmation of the prophet's truthfulness, so lying is impossible. Second, infallibility from major sins (kabā'ir) and base minor sins (ṣaghā'ir al-khissa) is established by consensus (ijmāʿ). Third, infallibility from all other sins (sā'ir al-dhunūb) is also affirmed, because the prophets are sent as exemplars; the people are commanded to follow them, and God does not command what is sinful. Thus prophets are protected from all sin.

Key Terms
صدق الرسل
عصمتهم
الضرورة
المعجزة
الإجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophetic infallibility is limited only to major sins, not minor slips.
Correction: Sanusi includes protection from all sins, including base minor sins, and argues that prophets are sinless in all actions because they are exemplars.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, how is a prophet's truthfulness known?
A) By transmitted reports alone
B) Necessarily (ḍarūra) for every divinely guided person
C) By rational proof only
D) By consensus of the community

Key Takeaway
Prophets are truthful and infallible: truthfulness is self-evident, and infallibility covers all sins, proven by miracle, consensus, and the necessity of emulation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was free from sin? If so, how does that change the way you view his Sunnah in your daily life? Are you emulating him with the same level of commitment as if he were infallible in every matter? What specific area of your life do you need to align more closely with his example?
?
The passage says that prophetic truthfulness is 'known necessarily'. Is that really the case in your heart? Have you ever doubted the truthfulness of a prophetic report because it conflicts with your desires? Examine yourself: do you accept the Prophet's words as unquestionably true, or do you rationalise exceptions? Commit to one specific prophetic teaching you have been hesitant to follow and decide to act on it today.
?
If prophets are infallible from all sins, then they are perfect role models. What does that mean for your excuses when you fail to follow their example? Are you willing to hold yourself to the standard of the prophet in a specific situation this week, knowing that he never sinned? Write down one situation where you normally compromise and resolve to follow the prophetic model perfectly, seeking Allah's help.

Superiority of Muhammad and the Quran
Sanusi declares Muhammad the best prophet and the Quran the greatest miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Prophet Muhammad is the best of all prophets, sent to all humanity, and that the Quran is his greatest miracle, still evident today.

Core Idea
Muhammad is the best prophet and the Quran is the eternal miracle.

Sanusi establishes two key aspects of Muhammad's prophethood: his superiority over all other prophets and the universal scope of his mission. He then highlights the Quran as the greatest and most enduring miracle, one that can be rationally perceived at any time. This lesson unpacks these foundational beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Read the declaration
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi begins with 'And the best of them' referring to prophets.
The phrase 'أفضلهم' sets the tone for the entire passage.
2
Identify the three claims
Identify the three claims made: Muhammad's superiority, his universal mission, and the Quran as his greatest miracle.
These are the three main points.
3
Reflect on the Quran's miracle
Consider why Sanusi says the Quran's inimitability is 'perceived by direct observation until now.' What does that mean for believers today?
This underscores the Quran's ongoing relevance and miraculous nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفضلهم نبينا وسيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلَّمَ ، بعثَهُ الله سبحانَهُ إلى أهلِ الأَرضِ كافَّةً ، وأَيَّدَهُ بمعجزات لا حصر لها ، وأفضلها القرآن العظيم الذي إعجازه للخَلْقَ مُدْرَكُ بالعِيان إلى الآن
And the best of them is our Prophet, our Master, and our Liege Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. God, glorified be He, sent him to all people of the earth, and supported him with countless miracles, the greatest of which is the Magnificent Quran, whose inimitability (iʿjāz) for creation is perceived by direct observation until now.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a declaration of the superiority of Prophet Muhammad over all other prophets and the uniqueness of his primary miracle, the Quran. Sanusi begins by affirming that the best (afḍal) of all prophets is our Prophet Muhammad (SAW). He then notes three key aspects: first, his universal mission — he was sent to all people of the earth, not just a specific nation. Second, he was supported by miracles without count (lā ḥaṣr lahā), meaning an immense number. Third, the greatest of these miracles is the Quran, which Sanusi describes as 'the Magnificent' (al-ʿaẓīm). Its miraculous inimitability (iʿjāz) is perceived by direct observation (bil-ʿiyān) and continues to be so until the present day. This means the Quran's challenge remains open, and its inimitability is evident to all who reflect.

Key Terms
أفضل الرسل
بعثه إلى أهل الأرض كافة
معجزة
إعجاز القرآن
العيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that miracles only occurred during the Prophet's lifetime and are no longer available.
Correction: Sanusi states that the Quran's inimitability is perceived by direct observation until now, meaning it is an ongoing miracle.

Checkpoint
What does Sanusi say about the Quran's miraculous nature?

B) It is perceived by direct observation and remains so until now
C) It is only known by transmitted reports
D) It is not a miracle but a metaphor

Key Takeaway
Prophet Muhammad is the best of all prophets, sent to all humanity, and the Quran remains his greatest miracle, evident to all who reflect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Quran's miraculous nature is 'perceptible until now'—when was the last time you sat with the Quran and felt its inimitability? If it's been a while, what is holding you back from truly engaging with it?
?
You are among 'all people of the earth' to whom Muhammad was sent. Have you fully embraced his message as your personal guide, or do you keep it at arm's length? Commit to one concrete action this week that shows you take his prophethood seriously.

Obligatory Beliefs about the Afterlife
Sanusi enumerates obligatory eschatological beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific eschatological beliefs that are obligatory to accept from the Prophet.

Core Idea
Resurrection, grave, bridge, balance, pool, intercession — all are unseen truths we must affirm.

Sanusi concludes his discussion on prophethood by asserting that everything the Prophet brought from God must be believed. He then enumerates key beliefs about the afterlife, emphasizing that they are matters of the unseen (sami'iyyat) that require assent. This passage clarifies what exactly a Muslim must affirm about the hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of eschatological items
Read the Arabic passage and translation, noting each item Sanusi mentions: resurrection, questioning in the grave, etc.
Notice how he uses 'like' (نحوه) to connect them.
2
Identify the consensus markers
Sanusi uses 'by consensus' (إجماعاً) for resurrection of the identical body and for intercession for sinful believers. Why does he emphasize consensus?
This shows these are agreed-upon doctrines.
3
Understand the nature of these beliefs
These are sam'iyyat — known through revelation, not reason. Reflect on the role of faith in accepting them.
4
Appreciate the precision
Sanusi specifies 'this very body' for resurrection, rejecting the idea of a similar body. This matters for the doctrine of bodily resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوجب تصديقه صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في كل ما أتى به عن الله تعالى ؛ كالبعثِ لعين هذا البدنِ لا لمثلِهِ إجماعاً ونحوه مِنْ سؤالِ القبرِ ونعيمِهِ وعذابِهِ ، والصراط . والميزان ، والحوضِ ، والشفاعة للعصاة المؤمنين في إنقاذهم مِنَ النارِ بعد نفوذ الوعيدِ في جماعة منهم إجماعاً ، وتأبيد نعيم المؤمنين وعذابِ الكافرين . ومعرفة تفاصيل ما أتى بهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مُبيَّنٌ في كتب الأئمةِ مِنَ الفقه والحديث . والقَصْدُ بهذهِ العُجالةِ إنَّما هو ذكرُ ما يَخرجُ بِهِ المكلَّفُ التقليدِ في العقائدِ ، وفَهْمُ هذهِ الجُمَلِ وافٍ بذلكَ إِنْ يسَّرَ الله سبحانَهُ أَتمَّ وفاء . وهو جلَّ وعلا المستعانُ والمسؤولُ أنْ يخرجنا بفضلِهِ ويُخرج بنا مِنَ الظلماتِ إلى النور ، وأن يكرمنا ويكرم على أيدينا بما يُوجِبُ لنا ولأحبَّتِنا مِنَ التنعم في أعلى الفردوس بشريف معرفتِهِ ولذيذ رؤيتِهِ أعظم سرورٍ ، وصلَّى الله على سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد عدد ما ذكرَهُ الذاكرونَ ، وغفل عن ذكره الغافلونَ ، ورضي الله تعالى عن أصحاب رسولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ أجمعين ، والحمد لله رب العالمين .
Thus it is obligatory to believe him, may God bless him and grant him peace, in everything he brought from God Most High: such as the resurrection of this very body, not a likeness of it, by consensus; and similar things like the questioning of the grave, its bliss and its torment; and the Bridge, and the Balance, and the Pool, and intercession for sinful believers to rescue them from the Fire after the threat has taken effect upon a group of them, by consensus; and the everlasting bliss of believers and torment of disbelievers. And knowledge of the details of what he, may God bless him and grant him peace, brought is explained in the books of the imams of jurisprudence and hadith. And the purpose of this brief treatise is only to mention what takes the responsible person out of blind imitation (taqlīd) in matters of creed, and understanding these sentences suffices for that, if God glorified facilitates complete fulfillment. And He, exalted and majestic, is the One whose help is sought and the One asked that He bring us out by His grace and bring out others through us from darkness to light, and that He honor us and honor through our hands what necessitates for us and for our loved ones bliss in the highest Paradise, with the noble knowledge of Him and the delightful vision of Him, the greatest joy. And may God bless our Master and Liege Muhammad as many times as those who remember have remembered and those who are heedless have neglected to remember Him. And may God be pleased with all the Companions of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. And praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on prophethood and transitions to the purpose of the entire book. It can be divided into three parts. First, Sanusi states that it is obligatory (wajaba) to believe the Prophet in everything he brought from God. He lists key eschatological beliefs: resurrection of the identical body (not a similar one, by consensus), the questioning in the grave, its bliss and punishment, the Bridge (Ṣirāṭ), the Balance (Mīzān), the Pool (Ḥawḍ), and intercession (Shafāʿa) for sinful believers after some have already been punished (by consensus). Also everlasting bliss for believers and everlasting punishment for disbelievers. These are details of the unseen (samiʿiyyāt) that must be accepted. Second, he notes that the full details are found in fiqh and hadith books, implying this treatise covers only essentials. Third, he states the purpose (qasd) of this 'brief treatise' (ʿujāla): to take the responsible person (mukallaf) out of blind imitation (taqlīd) in creed (ʿaqāʾid). Understanding these sentences (juman) suffices for that goal, if God facilitates. Finally, he ends with a supplication asking God to bring them out of darkness to light, to honor them and through them, and to grant them the highest Paradise with knowledge and vision of God, followed by blessings on the Prophet and satisfaction with the Companions. This reveals the author's deep personal devotion and his intent that the reader attain certain knowledge, not mere tradition.

Key Terms
تصديقه
البعث
سؤال القبر
الصراط
الميزان
الحوض
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that intercession is universal and all sinners will be saved unconditionally.
Correction: Sanusi specifies that intercession is only for sinful believers after the threat has taken effect on a group of them; it does not mean everyone is saved.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does 'by consensus' (ijma'an) specifically apply to?
A) The general obligation to believe the Prophet
B) Resurrection of this very body and intercession for sinful believers
C) The questioning in the grave
D) The everlasting bliss and torment

Key Takeaway
The eschatological beliefs listed by Sanusi are obligatory to affirm exactly as revealed, with consensus on the physical resurrection and intercession for sinful believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sanusi says resurrection is of 'this very body.' If you knew your body would return exactly as it is, would you change how you treat it today? What would you do differently starting now?
?
The Prophet's intercession is for sinful believers, but only after some have been punished. Does this make you more hopeful or more fearful? Are you relying on his intercession while neglecting your own repentance?
?
The Balance weighs deeds. If your deeds were weighed tonight, would the scale tip towards good or evil based on this lesson's content? What is one specific deed you can do today to tip the scale?

The Purpose of This Book: Leaving Taqlid in Creed
Sanusi states the purpose of his treatise and concludes with a supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sanusi wrote this treatise and what it means to move from blind imitation to personal conviction in beliefs.

Core Idea
This book is a guide to leave taqlid and achieve certain knowledge of creed.

After presenting the essential beliefs, Sanusi explains the purpose of his brief work: to help the responsible person (mukallaf) exit the state of blind imitation (taqlid) in matters of creed. He expresses hope that understanding these concise sentences will be sufficient. This reveals the pedagogical intention behind the entire text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the book's purpose
Read from 'Wa ma'rifatu tafasili...' to the end of the book's aim.
2
Understand the concept of taqlid in creed
Sanusi wants to take the mukallaf out of taqlid, meaning blind following without evidence. In matters of creed, taqlid is generally not sufficient.
This is a key methodological point in kalam.
3
Reflect on the author's confidence
Sanusi says that understanding these sentences (juman) will suffice to achieve that goal, if God facilitates. This shows his belief in the power of concise argumentation.
4
Appreciate the supplication
The concluding prayer asks God to bring them out of darkness to light and to grant the highest Paradise with knowledge and vision of God. This connects the intellectual goal to spiritual aspiration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Finality of Prophethood and the Descent of Jesus
Sanusi explains 'Khatam al-Nabiyyin' and refutes the objection about Jesus' descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the descent of Jesus at the end of time does not contradict the finality of prophethood.

Core Idea
Jesus descends as a follower, not a prophet.

Sanusi explains the meaning of 'Khatam al-Nabiyyin' and addresses a common objection. The passage clarifies that prophethood ended with Muhammad, and Jesus' return is as a supporter of Islamic law, not a new prophet.

Guided Path
1
Understand the meaning of 'Khatam al-Nabiyyin'
Read the Arabic phrase and its translation. Note the two possible pronunciations (kasr or fatha on the ta) and the definition: the last prophet.
2
Recognize the logical implication
Since 'prophet' is more general than 'messenger', negating prophets automatically negates messengers. So no prophet or messenger after Muhammad.
3
Consider the objection about Jesus
Some might think the descent of Jesus contradicts finality. Hold that objection in mind as you read the response.
4
See the refutation
Jesus descends only as a supporter of Muhammad's law, acting as a member of his community, not to bring any change. He does not come as a prophet.
5
Appreciate the purpose of his descent
His descent is an aid to the community during trials and when the light of the Sharia is dimmed. It ends with a supplication for well-being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : خاتم النبيين بكسر التاء وفتحها أي آخرهم بحيث لا نبي بعده ويلزم منه أن لا رسول بعده لأن النبي أعم من الرسول ونفي الأعم يستلزم نفي الأخص ولا يعترض بنزول عيسى عليه السلام آخر الزمان لأنه إنما ينزل على أنه ناصر لشرع سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم معظم له عامل بمقتضاه كواحد من أمته لا على أن يبدل شيئا من شرعه الشريف بزيادة أو نقصان وإنما الله سبحانه أغاث بهذه الأمة عند تلاطم أمواج الفتن عليها وانخماد نور الشريعة المحمدية من أكثر البلاد نسأل الله تعالى العافية إلى الممات في ديننا ودنيانا
His saying: 'Khatam al-Nabiyyin' with kasr of the ta' and fatha of it, i.e., their last, such that there is no prophet after him, and it entails that there is no messenger after him because the prophet is more general than the messenger, and the negation of the more general necessitates the negation of the more specific. And do not object by the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, at the end of time, because he only descends as a supporter of the law of our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, magnifying him, acting according to its requirement as one of his community, not to change anything of his noble law by increase or decrease. But Allah, glorified, has aided this community by him at the time of surging waves of trials upon it and the extinction of the light of the Muhammadan law from most lands. We ask Allah, exalted, for well-being until death in our religion and our world.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase 'Khatam al-Nabiyyin' meaning the Seal of the Prophets. The author notes both possible pronunciations (kasr or fatha on the ta) and defines it as the last prophet, implying no prophet after him. Since prophet is a broader category than messenger, negating prophets also negates messengers. The author then addresses a potential objection: the descent of Jesus at the end of time. The response is that Jesus will not come with a new law but as a follower of Muhammad's law, supporting and magnifying it. His descent is a mercy from Allah to the community during trials, not a new prophethood. The passage concludes with a supplication for well-being.

Misconception: Some think that the descent of Jesus at the end of time means he is a new prophet or messenger after Muhammad.
Correction: Jesus descends only as a supporter of Muhammad's law, acting as a member of the community, not to bring a new law or prophethood.

Meaning of 'Imam al-Mursalin' and Its Implication
Sanusi explains 'Imam al-Mursalin' can mean master or prayer leader, emphasizing the Prophet's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible meanings of the title 'Imam al-Mursalin' and why the phrase emphasizes the Prophet's superiority over all messengers.

Core Idea
'Imam al-Mursalin' can mean both master and prayer leader, both affirming the Prophet's unmatched rank.

Sanusi unpacks the title 'Imam al-Mursalin' (Imam of the Messengers) used for the Prophet Muhammad. He offers two interpretations: 'imam' as master or as prayer leader, grounding the latter in the Isra' hadith. The choice of 'messengers' over 'prophets' is intentional, as it underscores the Prophet's excellence even over the most distinguished group.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two interpretations
Read the passage carefully and identify the two possible meanings Sanusi gives for 'imam' in 'Imam al-Mursalin'.
One is apparent meaning, the other is metaphorical as 'master'.
2
Note the evidence for prayer leadership
Sanusi mentions the hadith of al-Isra' as proof for the literal interpretation of prayer leadership.
3
Reflect on the choice of 'al-mursalin'
Consider why Sanusi says 'al-mursalin' is used here instead of 'al-nabiyyin' as in the previous title.
This choice highlights the Prophet's virtue over even the most specific group.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وإمام المرسلين يحتمل أن يكون الإمام هنا بمعنى السيد ويحتمل أن يكون على ظاهره من إمامته لهم في الصلاة وقد ثبت ذلك من حديث الإسراء وإنما قال هنا : المرسلين ولم يقل : النبيين كما في الأول لأنه هنا فيه تقرير فضله ولا شك أنه إذا ثبت شفوفه وزيادة شرفه على المرسلين مع خصوصيتهم كان ثبوت ذلك
His saying: 'And Imam of the Messengers' – it is possible that 'imam' here means master, and it is possible that it is on its apparent meaning of his leading them in prayer, and that has been established from the hadith of al-Isra'. And he only said here: 'the messengers' and did not say 'the prophets' as in the first, because here is a confirmation of his virtue, and there is no doubt that when his excellence and increase of honor over the messengers with their specificity is established, the establishment of that...
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage explains the phrase 'Imam al-Mursalin' (Imam of the Messengers). The author offers two possible interpretations: 'imam' could mean 'master' (sayyid) or it could be taken literally as leading them in prayer, citing the Hadith of al-Isra' where the Prophet led the prophets in prayer. The author notes that the phrase uses 'al-mursalin' (messengers) rather than 'al-nabiyyin' (prophets) as in the earlier phrase 'Khatam al-Nabiyyin', because here the context is establishing the Prophet's virtue. If his excellence over the messengers is proven despite their special status, then this excellence is all the more clear.

Correction: Sanusi explicitly states that 'imam' can also mean prayer leader, and this is supported by the hadith of al-Isra'.

Key Takeaway

Explanation of 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' and the Objection of Jesus's Descent
Sanusi explains 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' and refutes the objection about Jesus's descent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the title 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' implies finality of prophethood and messengers, and how the future descent of Jesus does not contradict this.

Core Idea
The Seal of Prophethood means no prophet or messenger comes after Muhammad — not even Jesus returns as a prophet.

In this passage, Sanusi explains the meaning of 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' as the last of the prophets, and draws the logical conclusion that no messenger can come after him either. He then addresses a common objection: the anticipated descent of Jesus at the end of time. Understanding this refutation is key to preserving the doctrine of Muhammad's finality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the linguistic clarification and logical flow.
2
Follow the logical reasoning
Identify how Sanusi uses the generality of 'prophet' over 'messenger' to conclude that no messenger can come after Muhammad.
The phrase 'negation of the more general necessitates negation of the more specific' is a key logical principle.
3
Understand the refutation
Examine why the descent of Jesus does not break the seal. Note that Jesus descends as a supporter and follower, not as a new prophet or lawgiver.
This refutation is essential for defending the doctrine of finality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( خاتم النبيينَ ) بكسر التاء وفتحها ؛ أي : آخرهم ؛ بحيثُ لا نبي بعده ، ويلزم منه أن لا رسولَ بعدَهُ ؛ لأنَّ النبيَّ أعم مِنَ الرسولِ ، ونفي الأعم يستلزم نفي الأخص . ولا يُعترَضُ بنزول عيسى عليهِ السلامُ آخر الزمانِ ؛ لأَنَّهُ إِنَّما يَنزِلُ على أنَّه ناصر لشرع سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلَّمَ ، مُعظم له ، عامل بمقتضاه كواحدٍ مِنْ أُمَّتِهِ ، لا على أنْ يُبدِّلَ شيئاً مِنْ شرعِهِ الشريف بزيادة أو نقصان ، وإِنَّما الله سبحانَهُ أَغاثَ بهِ هذه الأمَّةَ عندَ تلاطم أمواج الفتنِ عليها ، وانخمادِ نور الشريعة المحمَّديَّةِ مِنْ أكثرِ البلادِ ، نسألُ الله تعالى العافية إلى المماتِ في ديننا ودنيانا
His statement: (Khatam an-Nabiyyin) with kasr of the tā' and its fatḥ; meaning: their last; such that there is no prophet after him, and it necessarily follows that there is no messenger after him, because the prophet is more general than the messenger, and the negation of the more general necessitates the negation of the more specific. And it is not objected to by the descent of Jesus, peace be upon him, at the end of time; because he only descends as a supporter of the law of our master and patron Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, magnifying him, acting according to its requirements as one of his community, not so that he changes anything of his noble law by increase or decrease. Rather, God, exalted is He, brings relief through him to this community at the time of the clashing of waves of tribulations upon it and the extinguishing of the light of the Muhammadian law in most lands. We ask God, exalted is He, for well-being until death in our religion and our world.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and defense of the title 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' (Seal of the Prophets) applied to Prophet Muhammad. The commentator first clarifies the linguistic variants (kasar or fatḥ on the tā' of 'khatam') and defines the term as 'their last', meaning no prophet comes after him. He then draws a logical implication: since a prophet is more general than a messenger (every messenger is a prophet but not vice versa), negating the existence of any prophet after Muhammad also negates any messenger. Next, he addresses a common objection: the future descent of Jesus (ʿĪsā) at the end of time. He explains that Jesus will not come as a new prophet or messenger, but as a follower of Muhammad's law, supporting and magnifying it, acting like any other member of the Muslim community. He will not alter the law by addition or subtraction. The reason for his descent is that God will send him as a relief for the community during intense tribulations and when the light of the Sharia has dimmed in many lands. The passage ends with a supplication for well-being in religion and worldly life.

Key Terms
خاتم النبيين
نبي
رسول
عيسى عليه السلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jesus will return as a new prophet, contradicting Muhammad's finality.
Correction: Jesus returns not as a prophet but as a follower of Muhammad's law, acting as a member of his community.

Checkpoint
What logical implication does the commentator draw from the phrase 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin' regarding messengers?
A) Messengers can still come after Muhammad.
B) Since prophets are more general, negating prophets also negates messengers.
C) The phrase only applies to prophets, not messengers.
D) Jesus will come as a new messenger.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad is the last prophet and messenger; Jesus will return not as a prophet but as a follower of Muhammad's law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as though Muhammad is the final messenger, or do you sometimes look to other sources (philosophers, modern gurus, cultural trends) as if they can add to or modify his law? What would change if you fully submitted to his finality?
?
Jesus will descend as a follower of Muhammad's law, not a lawgiver. How does this reality challenge your ego when you are tempted to innovate or prioritize your own opinions over the clear rulings of the Sharia?
?

The Meaning of 'Imam al-Mursalin' and its Significance
Sanusi explains the title and its theological implication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible interpretations of 'imam' in this title and why the title uses 'al-Mursalin' rather than 'an-Nabiyyin' to assert Muhammad's supreme virtue.

Core Idea
Muhammad's leadership over messengers proves his superiority over all prophets.

Sanusi now turns to the title 'Imam al-Mursalin' (Leader of the Messengers), found in the prayer on the Prophet. This title is not merely descriptive; it carries theological weight about Muhammad's rank. The commentator unpacks two possible meanings of 'imam' and then explains why the title specifies 'messengers' rather than the broader 'prophets' — a choice that sharpens the argument for the Prophet's unmatched excellence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once, then the literal translation. Notice the two possibilities for 'imam' and the logical argument at the end.
The passage uses a conditional reasoning: if superiority over messengers, then over prophets even more.
2
Understand the two meanings of 'imam'
Identify both interpretations: imam as 'master' or imam as 'prayer leader'. Note that the second is supported by the hadith of Isra'.
Both meanings affirm leadership, but the prayer-leader interpretation is specific.
3
Analyze the choice of 'al-Mursalin'
Ask why 'messengers' instead of 'prophets'. The answer: to emphasize virtue over the highest category.
Messengers are the elite among prophets; superiority over them implies superiority over all.
4
Trace the logical argument
Follow the reasoning: if Muhammad is preeminent over messengers (despite their specificity), then it is even more fitting that he is preeminent over other prophets.
This is an a fortiori (first, then even more) argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإمام المرسلينَ ) يحتملُ أنْ يكونَ الإمامُ هنا بمعنى السيد ، ويحتمل أَنْ يكونَ على ظاهرِهِ مِنْ إمامته لهم في الصلاة وقد ثبت ذلكَ مِنْ حديثِ الإسراء وإنما قال هنا : ( المرسلين ) ، ولم يقل : ( النبيِّينَ ) كما في الأول ؛ لأنَّه هنا فيه تقرير فضلِهِ ، ولا شكّ أَنَّهُ إِذا ثبت شفوفه وزيادة شرفِهِ على المرسلينَ معَ خصوصيَّتِهم .. كانَ ثبوت ذلكَ أحرى وأولى فيمَنْ ثبت له مطلقُ النبوَّةِ .
His statement: (And the Imam of the Messengers). It is possible that 'imam' here means the master, and it is possible that it is according to its apparent meaning of his leading them in prayer, and that has been established from the hadith of al-Isra'. And he only said here 'al-Mursalin' (the messengers) and did not say 'an-Nabiyyin' (the prophets) as in the first, because here there is confirmation of his virtue. And there is no doubt that if his preeminence and increase of honor over the messengers, despite their specificity, is established, then its establishment is more fitting and more appropriate for one for whom absolute prophethood is established.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the title 'Imam al-Mursalin' (Leader of the Messengers). The commentator gives two possible interpretations: 'imam' could mean 'sayyid' (master), or it could be taken literally as leading them in prayer, which is confirmed by the hadith of the Night Journey (Isra'). He then notes that the title uses 'al-Mursalin' (messengers) rather than 'an-Nabiyyin' (prophets) as in the previous title 'Khatam an-Nabiyyin'. The reason is that this title is about affirming Muhammad's virtue (faḍl). The argument is: if Muhammad's preeminence (shufūf) and increase in honor over the messengers—who are the elite among prophets—is established, then it is even more fitting and prior that such virtue be established for those who only have absolute prophethood (i.e., non-messenger prophets). In other words, superiority over messengers implies superiority over all prophets.

Key Terms
إمام المرسلين
شفوف
زيادة شرف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think 'imam' here refers only to leading prayer, limiting its significance.
Correction: The commentator allows both interpretations—imam as master or as prayer leader—and both affirm Muhammad's leadership.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say 'al-Mursalin' here rather than 'an-Nabiyyin'?
A) The first title already used 'an-Nabiyyin'.
B) To emphasize Muhammad's virtue over the highest category.
C) It is a grammatical requirement.
D) It refers only to messengers among the prophets.

Key Takeaway
Muhammad's title 'Imam al-Mursalin' establishes his superiority over all prophets through a logical argument starting from the highest rank of messengers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Muhammad's superiority over the best of creation is established, how does that affect your own estimation of his teachings and your commitment to following them? Will you let this truth change how you prioritize his sunnah today?
?
You claim to love the Prophet, but do you truly acknowledge his rank as the Imam over every messenger? What specific action will you take this week to show that you accept his leadership over all other authorities in your life?
?
The a fortiori argument: if he is greater than the greatest, then surely he is greater than everyone. Does your heart truly place him above every desire, opinion, and person? What is one area where you still put someone else's word above his?

Linguistic Meanings of Prophet and Messenger
Definition of prophet and messenger with linguistic derivations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible linguistic derivations of the word 'prophet' (nabī) and the basic meaning of 'messenger' (rasūl) in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
The word 'prophet' can mean either 'informed one' or 'elevated one' — and both fit.

Sanusi begins by clarifying the key terms before any theological discussion can proceed. He cites Qadi Iyad to explain that 'nubuwwa' derives either from 'nabā'' (news) or 'nabwa' (height), while 'rasūl' simply means 'one sent' with the duty of conveying. This linguistic groundwork sets the stage for understanding their relationship.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage once focusing on the two derivations for 'nabī' and the description of 'rasūl'.
2
Understand the two origins of 'nabī'
Notice that for those who hamzah, it comes from 'nabā'' meaning news; for those who don't, it comes from 'nabwa' meaning elevation. Both lead to the idea of a high rank.
Qadi Iyad shows they are harmonious.
3
Analyze the meaning of 'rasūl'
The messenger is one sent with a command to convey. The form fa'ūl is rare for maf'ūl.
The derivation from 'tatābu'' implies repetition of conveying.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بدَّ مِنْ بيان معنى النبي ومعنى النبوَّة شرعاً ، ومعنى الرسول أيضاً ، وبيان ما قيل في الوصفينِ مِنَ التساوي والفرق .
قال القاضي عياض رحمهُ اللهُ تعالى : ( النبوَّةُ في لغةِ مَنْ همَزَ : مِنَ النبأ ؛ أي : الخبرِ ، وقد لا تُهمَزُ تسهيلاً ) ، فسُمِّيَ النبيُّ على هذا نبيئاً ؛ بمعنى : أنَّ الله تعالى أطلعَهُ على غَيْبِهِ ، وأعلمَهُ أَنَّهُ فنبيء : فعيل بمعنى مفعول ؛ أي : مُنيَّاً ، أو بمعنى فاعل ؛ أي : مُخبِرٍ عن الله تعالى بما بعثَهُ بهِ وأطلعَهُ عليهِ
وعندَ مَنْ لم يَهمِزْ : مِنَ النَّبْوَةِ ؛ أي : ما ارتفعَ مِنَ الأرضِ . ومعناه : المرتبة الشريفة ، فالنبي له مرتبة شريفة منيفة عند مولاه ، فالوصفانِ مؤتلفان
وأَمَّا الرسولُ : فمعناه : المرسَلُ ، ولم يَأْتِ فَعُولٌ بمعنى مُفعَل إلا نادراً ، وإرساله : أمرُ اللهِ تعالى له بالإبلاغ للخلْقِ
•
واشتقاقُهُ : مِنَ التتابع (٢) ؛ يُقالُ : جاءَ الناسُ أرسالاً يتبع بعضُهم بعضاً ؛ كأنَّهُ أُلزِمَ تكرير التبليغ ، والزِمَتِ الأُمَّةُ اتِّباعَهُ
وقيل : النبي والرسول مترادفان
وقيل : اجتمعا في النبوة بالمعنيين المتقدمينِ ، وزاد الرسولُ بالأمر بالإنذار (1)
وقيل : زادَ بمجيئه بشرع مبتدأ ، ومَنْ لم يأتِ بِهِ فنبي غيرُ رسول
وإِنْ أُمِرَ بالإبلاغ والإنذار .
ومذهب الأكثرين : أنَّ كلَّ رسول نبي ، ولا عكس .
وأوَّلُ الرُّسُلِ : آدم ، وآخِرُهم : سيّدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى الله وسلَّمَ عليه وعليهم أجمعينَ ، وفي حديث أبي ذر رضي الله عنه : الأَنْبِيَاءُ مِنَهُ أَلْفِ وَأَرْبَعَةٌ وَثَلَاثُونَ أَلفاً ، وَالرُّسُلُ مِنْهُمْ ثَلَاثُ مِئَةٍ وَثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ ، أَوَّلُهُمْ آدَمُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ (۲)
قالوا : ويخرجُ عددهم أجمعينَ مِنِ اسم سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ (۳)
ثم النبوَّةُ والرسالة ليستا ذاتاً للنبي ولا وصف ذات(٤) ، بل
It is necessary to explain the meaning of prophet (nabī) and the meaning of prophethood (nubuwwa) in Islamic law, and also the meaning of messenger (rasūl), and to explain what has been said about the two descriptions regarding equivalence and difference. Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ (may God have mercy on him) said: 'Prophethood in the language of those who hamzah is from nabāʾ, meaning news, and sometimes it is not hamzated for ease.' So the prophet is called nabīʾ on this basis, meaning that God Almighty informed him of His unseen and made known to him that he is a nabīʾ: faʿīl in the sense of mafʿūl, i.e., one who is informed (munabbaʾ), or in the sense of fāʿil, i.e., one who informs (mukhbir) about God Almighty with what He sent him and informed him. According to those who do not hamzah, it is from nabwa, meaning what is elevated from the earth. Its meaning is the noble rank. So the prophet has a noble and exalted rank with his Lord. Thus the two descriptions are harmonious. As for the messenger, his meaning is the one sent (mursal), and the form faʿūl in the sense of mufʿal is rare. His being sent (irsāl) is God Almighty's command to him to convey (iblāgh) to creation. Its derivation is from t-tābaʿ (sequence); it is said: 'The people came in successive groups (arsālan), one after another,' as if he is required to repeat the conveying, and the community is required to follow him. It is said that prophet and messenger are synonymous. It is said that they share in prophethood with the two preceding meanings, and the messenger is increased by the command to warn (indhār). It is said that he is increased by his coming with a new revealed law (sharʿ mubtadaʾ), and whoever does not bring one is a prophet but not a messenger, even if he is commanded to convey and warn. The majority view is that every messenger is a prophet, but not vice versa. The first of the messengers is Adam, and the last of them is our master and patron Muḥammad (may God bless and salute him and all of them). In the hadith of Abū Dharr (may God be pleased with him): 'The prophets from him are one hundred and twenty-four thousand, and the messengers from them are three hundred and thirteen. The first of them is Adam, peace be upon him.' They said: Their total number emerges from the name of our master and patron Muḥammad (may God bless and salute him). Then prophethood and messengership (risāla) are not an essence (dhāt) of the prophet nor an attribute of essence (ṣifat dhāt), but...
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory discussion of the terms 'prophet' (nabī) and 'messenger' (rasūl) in Islamic theology. The author begins by stating the need to explain the legal (sharʿī) meanings of prophethood (nubuwwa) and messenger (rasūl), and to clarify whether they are equivalent or different. He then cites Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ's linguistic analysis: for those who pronounce the hamzah, 'nubuwwa' derives from 'nabāʾ' (news), so the prophet is one who is informed by God or one who informs about God. For those who do not hamzah, it derives from 'nabwa' (elevation), indicating a high rank. Both interpretations are harmonious. Next, he defines 'rasūl' as 'one sent' (mursal), noting that the form faʿūl in the sense of mafʿūl is rare. 'Irsāl' (sending) means God's command to convey (iblāgh) to creation. The derivation is from 'tatābuʿ' (succession), implying the messenger is required to repeatedly convey, and the community must follow. The author then presents three opinions on the relationship: (1) the terms are synonymous; (2) they share in prophethood but the messenger is distinguished by the command to warn (indhār); (3) the messenger brings a new revealed law (sharʿ mubtadaʾ), while a prophet who does not bring a new law is not a messenger, even if commanded to convey and warn. The majority view is that every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger. The passage then states that the first messenger is Adam and the last is Muhammad, and cites a hadith giving numerical counts: 124,000 prophets, 313 messengers, and that the total number can be derived from the name Muhammad by abjad calculation. Finally, the author begins to assert that prophethood and messengership are not essential attributes of the prophet (i.e., they are not part of his essence or an inseparable attribute), but this sentence is cut off at the page end.

نبوة

A) From 'nabā'' meaning news

D) From 'risāla' meaning message

Key Takeaway
The terms 'prophet' and 'messenger' have distinct linguistic origins that inform their theological significance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophet is both informed and elevated. Which aspect do you neglect more in your relationship with the Prophet ﷺ: seeking to know his message (the 'news' he brought) or honoring his elevated rank in your heart? What concrete step will you take today to address that neglect?
?
The term 'rasūl' implies repeated conveying. How often do you listen to the message of the Messenger ﷺ as if it is being sent to you anew each day? When was the last time you truly felt the urgency of his call in your life? What will you do to make this message fresh for you tomorrow?
?
The two derivations of 'nabī' are harmonious. Are there aspects of your life where you treat knowledge of Islam and reverence for its figures as separate or even contradictory? How can you integrate both this week?

Relationship Between Prophethood and Messengership
Classification of opinions on prophet vs messenger and majority view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different scholarly opinions on whether 'prophet' and 'messenger' are synonymous or distinct, and the majority view that every messenger is a prophet but not vice versa.

Core Idea
Every messenger is a prophet, but not every prophet is a messenger.

Having established the linguistic meanings, Sanusi now turns to the theological relationship between prophethood and messengership. He presents several opinions, from complete synonymy to the view that a messenger brings a new law, and concludes with the majority position.

Guided Path
1
Read the opinions on synonymy
Notice the three views: synonymous, shared but messenger warns, and messenger brings new law.
2
Identify the majority view
The passage states that the majority holds that every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger.
This is a key distinction.
3
Note the numerical information
The hadith gives numbers of prophets and messengers, and the first and last messengers are named.
The total number is said to be derived from the name Muhammad.

Prophet and Messenger: Distinction and Majority View
Sanusi presents various opinions on the nabi-rasul distinction and the majority view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the relationship between prophethood and messengerhood according to Sunni theology, the majority view that every messenger is a prophet but not vice versa, and the refutation of the Karramiyya who considered these roles essential attributes.

Core Idea
Prophethood and messengerhood are divine designations, not essential attributes.

Sanusi presents different scholarly opinions on the distinction between a prophet and a messenger. He clarifies the majority position that every messenger is a prophet but not vice versa, cites a hadith on their numbers, and refutes the Karramiyya who considered prophethood and messengerhood essential attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translation to absorb its rhythm. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: opinions, majority view, hadith, refutation.
The passage is dense but logically ordered.
2
Identify the two reported opinions
The passage begins with two opinions on the nabi-rasul distinction. Find them and note how they differ: the first focuses on the command to warn, the second on bringing a new law.
These are not the majority view.
3
Understand the majority view
The majority holds that every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger. This is the key hierarchy. Memorize it as a principle.
This is the orthodox Sunni position.
4
Reflect on the hadith and refutation
Note the hadith numbers for prophets and messengers, and the claim that their total is derived from Muhammad's name. Then understand the refutation of the Karramiyya: nubuwwa and risala are not essential attributes but divine selections.
This refutes a sectarian error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل : اجتمعا في النبوة بالمعنيين المتقدمينِ ، وزاد الرسولُ بالأمر بالإنذار وقيل : زادَ بمجيئه بشرع مبتدأ ، ومَنْ لم يأتِ بِهِ فنبي غيرُ رسول وإن أُمِرَ بالإبلاغ والإنذار . ومذهب الأكثرين : أنَّ كلَّ رسول نبي ، ولا عكس . وأوَّلُ الرُّسُلِ : آدم ، وآخِرُهم : سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله وسلَّمَ عليه وعليهم أجمعينَ ، وفي حديث أبي ذر رضي الله عنه : الأَنْبِيَاءُ مِنْهُ أَلْفِ وَأَرْبَعَةٌ وَعِشْرُونَ أَلفاً ، وَالرُّسُلُ مِنْهُمْ ثَلَاثُ مِئَةٍ وَثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ ، أَوَّلُهُمْ آدَمُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ قالوا : ويخرجُ عددهم أجمعينَ مِنِ اسم سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ثم النبوَّةُ والرسالة ليستا ذاتاً للنبي ولا وصف ذات، بل تخصيص الله تعالى إيَّاهُ بذلكَ، خلافاً للكراميَّةِ أبعدهم الله تعالى
And it was said: They (the prophet and messenger) are united in prophethood according to the two preceding meanings, and the messenger is distinguished by the command to warn. And it was said: He is distinguished by coming with a new law, and whoever does not come with it is a prophet not a messenger, even if commanded to convey and warn. And the majority view: that every messenger is a prophet, but not vice versa. And the first messenger is Adam, and the last is our master and patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, upon him and upon them all. And in the hadith of Abu Dharr, may Allah be pleased with him: 'The prophets from him are one thousand and twenty-four thousand, and the messengers from them are three hundred and thirteen. The first of them is Adam, peace be upon him.' They said: And their total number is derived from the name of our master and patron Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Then prophethood and messengerhood are not an essence for the prophet nor an attribute of essence, but rather a specification by Allah the Exalted to him, contrary to the Karramiyya, may Allah distance them.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines the relationship between prophethood (nubuwwa) and messengerhood (risala). It begins by reporting two opinions: one that they share the same essential meaning but the messenger adds the command to warn, another that the messenger brings a new law while a prophet without a new law is still a prophet. Then it states the majority view that every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger. It then gives the first and last messengers (Adam and Muhammad) and cites a hadith with numbers of prophets and messengers. Finally, it explains that nubuwwa and risala are not essential attributes of the prophet's essence but are a specific designation from Allah, refuting the Karramiyya sect who considered them essential.

Key Terms
نبوة
رسالة
كرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophethood and messengerhood are essential attributes of a prophet's essence.
Correction: Sanusi states they are not essence or attribute of essence, but a specification from Allah, refuting the Karramiyya.

Checkpoint
According to the majority opinion presented, what is the relationship between a messenger (rasul) and a prophet (nabi)?
A) Every prophet is a messenger
B) Every messenger is a prophet, but not every prophet is a messenger
C) They are the same
D) A messenger is not necessarily a prophet

Key Takeaway
The majority view holds that every messenger is a prophet but not every prophet is a messenger, and these roles are divine selections not inherent qualities.

?

Prophethood

Al-Qarafi's Refutation of Prophethood as Mere Revelation
Al-Qarafi refutes the claim that prophethood is mere revelation and defines it precisely.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophethood cannot be equated with mere revelation and how al-Qarafi distinguishes prophecy from messengerhood based on the scope of the legislative command.

Core Idea
Prophethood is not any revelation; it is a specific legislative command tailored to the prophet alone.

Al-Qarafi begins by dismantling a widespread misconception that prophethood is simply any divine revelation. He points out that revelation occurs to non-prophets, such as Mary and the mother of Moses, proving that revelation alone is insufficient. He then presents the correct definition among verifying scholars: prophethood is a legislative judgment revealed specifically to the prophet, while messengerhood adds the obligation to convey that judgment to others. This passage sharpens our understanding of the distinct roles of prophets and messengers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the misconception
Read the first sentence to see what common belief al-Qarafi is refuting. Notice he calls it false.
The misconception is that prophethood is mere revelation.
2
Examine the counterexamples
Look at the examples of Mary, the mother of Moses, and the man in the hadith. Understand why they received revelation but were not prophets.
These examples show revelation can happen to non-prophets.
3
Understand the definition and distinction
Read the later part where al-Qarafi defines prophethood as a specific legislative revelation and distinguishes it from messengerhood by the scope of the command.
Note the example of 'Iqra' and 'Qum fa-andhir'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالَ القرافي : ( يعتقد كثيرٌ أنَّ النبوَّةَ مجرَّدُ الوحي ، وهو باطل ; لحصولِهِ لَمَنْ ليسَ بنبي ; كمريم وأُم موسى ، وليستا بنبيتين على الصحيح ، معَ أَنَّ الله تعالى يقولُ : فَأَرْسَلْنَا إِلَيْهَا رُوحَنَا ﴾ [مريم : ١٧] ، وفي « مسلم » : « بَعَثَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى مَلَكاً لِرَجُلٍ عَلَى مَدْرَجَتِهِ كَانَ خَرَجَ فِي زِيَارَةِ أَخٍ لَهُ فِي اللهِ تَعَالَى ، وَقَالَ لَهُ : إِنَّ اللَّهَ يُعْلِمُكَ أَنَّهُ يُحِبُّكَ ; لِحُبِّكَ لأَخِيكَ فِي اللهِ تَعَالَى ((۲) ، وليس بنبوة ; لأنَّها عندَ المُحقَّقينَ إيحاءُ اللهِ تعالى لبعض بحكم إنشائي يختص به ، كقوله : أقرأ بِاسْمِ رَبِّكَ ﴾ [العلق : ١] ، فهذا تكليف يختص بهِ في الوقتِ ، فهذهِ نبوَّة لا رسالة ، فلما نزلَتْ : ﴿ قُرْ فَأَنذِرُ ﴾ [المدثر : ٢] . . كانت رسالة ; لتعلُّق هذا التكليف بغيره أيضاً ; فالنبيُّ كُلَّفَ بما يخصه ، والرسولُ بذلك وتبليغه غيرَهُ ، فالرسولُ أخص مطلقاً )
And al-Qarafi said: 'Many believe that prophethood is mere revelation, and it is false, because it occurs to one who is not a prophet, like Mary and the mother of Moses, and they are not prophetesses according to the correct view, even though Allah the Exalted says: "We sent to her Our Spirit" [Maryam: 17]. And in Muslim: "Allah the Exalted sent an angel to a man on his path who had gone out to visit a brother for the sake of Allah the Exalted, and said to him: Indeed Allah informs you that He loves you, because of your love for your brother for the sake of Allah the Exalted." And this is not prophethood, because in the view of the verifying scholars it is Allah's revelation to someone of a legislative judgment specific to him, like His saying: "Recite in the name of your Lord" [Al-Alaq: 1]. So this is a task specific to him at that time, so this is prophethood not messengerhood. Then when "Arise and warn" [Al-Muddaththir: 2] was revealed, it became messengerhood because this command also concerns others. So the prophet is tasked with what is specific to him, and the messenger with that and its conveyance to others, so the messenger is more specific absolutely.'
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Qarafi refuting a common misconception that distinguishes prophethood (nubuwwa) from mere revelation (wahy). It presents a two-part argument: first, many people erroneously identify prophethood with any revelation, but this is false because revelation occurs to non-prophets like Mary and the mother of Moses. Even explicit angelic communication in the hadith about the man on his path does not constitute prophethood. Second, the correct definition among verifying scholars is that prophethood is a specific legislative revelation (īḥāʾ bi-ḥukm inshāʾī) exclusive to the prophet. The example of 'Iqraʾ' (Recite) is given: that command was specific to the Prophet at that time, making it prophethood. When the command 'Qum fa-andhir' (Arise and warn) came, it became messengerhood (risāla) because the command to warn involved others. Thus the prophet is charged only with what pertains to himself, while the messenger conveys that to others, making messengerhood more specific and inclusive.

Key Terms
نبوة
وحي
إيحاء
تكليف إنشائي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think prophethood is simply any divine revelation.
Correction: Al-Qarafi argues that revelation occurs to non-prophets, so prophethood must be a specific legislative judgment from Allah.

Checkpoint
Why does al-Qarafi reject the idea that prophethood is mere revelation?
A) Because revelation is impossible
B) Because revelation occurs to non-prophets like Mary and the mother of Moses
C) Because prophethood does not involve revelation
D) Because revelation is only for angels

Key Takeaway
Prophethood is not mere revelation but a specific legislative command from Allah to the prophet alone, while messengerhood includes conveying that command to others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Qur'an, do you treat each command as a personal, legislative decree from Allah to you, just as the Prophet received 'Iqra' as a command specific to him? Or do you read it as information, letting it pass without feeling the weight of obligation? What would change if you received every verse as a direct command to your soul?
?
The Prophet's prophethood began with a command for himself, and only later he was commanded to warn others. Are you living your faith merely as a personal relationship with Allah, or have you accepted the responsibility to convey the truth to those around you—even when it requires courage? If you have not, what is holding you back?
?
Al-Qarafi warns against confusing mere inspiration with prophethood. Have you ever assumed that a strong feeling, a dream, or an inner conviction was a direct message from Allah? How can you ensure you do not elevate your own impressions to the level of divine legislation, and instead submit to the clear commands of the Qur'an and Sunnah as your only binding guidance?

The Qur'anic Proof of the World's Origination via Appearance and Disappearance
The author introduces the Qur'anic basis for the proof and begins the logical inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the rational proof for the world's origination is rooted in the Qur'anic argument of Abraham, using the concepts of appearance and disappearance.

Core Idea
The Qur'anic proof is rational: appearance and disappearance prove origination.

In this lesson, we will see how the author connects the rational proof of the world's origination (huduth al-alam) to the Qur'anic narrative of Prophet Abraham. Abraham inferred the origination of celestial bodies from their alternating appearance and disappearance, an argument that parallels the earlier proof from motion and rest. By grounding the rational proof in revelation, the author demonstrates the harmony between reason and scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English carefully to get the flow of the argument. Notice the key terms.
Pay attention to the phrase 'الظهور والأفول نظير الحركة والسكون' which establishes the analogy.
2
Understand the analogy
The author compares appearing/disappearing to motion/rest. Consider why this analogy is important for proving origination—both involve change over time.
3
Follow the logical inference
The passage begins the argument: if a celestial body existed in preeternity, it would have to be either always apparent or always non-apparent. The passage states that being always apparent is impossible because then it would never disappear as observed.
The argument is incomplete here; it continues on the next page, but you can grasp the core premise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع في رجوع برهان حدوث العالم إلى القرآن الكريم ] هذا البرهانُ الذي سلكناه في حدوثِ العالم : هو مقتبس مِنَ البرهان الذي أشار إليهِ القرآنُ حكاية عن خليل الله إبراهيم على نبينا وعليه الصلاة والسلام ؛ أعني : الذي استدل به على حدوثِ الكوكب والقمر والشمس ؛ وهو ظهورها تارةً ، وأفولها أخرى ، فالظهور والأفولُ نظيرُ الحركة والسكون ؛ فيُقالُ في الاستدلال على حدوثِ تلك الأجرامِ بالظهورِ والأُفول : لو كان شيء منها موجوداً في الأزلِ لم يخلُ : إما أن يكون ظاهراً ، أو آفلاً ، والملازمة ظاهرةٌ ؛ إذ لا واسطة بينَ الظُّهورِ والأُفول ، وكونُ ذلكَ الجِرْمِ في الأزلِ ظاهراً مستحيل ، وإلا لزم أن يبقى ظاهراً أبداً ؛
The Fourth: On the Return of the Proof of the Origination of the World to the Noble Qur'an. This proof that we have followed concerning the origination of the world (huduth al-'alam) is derived from the proof that the Qur'an indicated narrating from the Friend of God, Abraham (Ibrahim), peace and blessings be upon our Prophet and upon him; that is, the one he used to infer the origination of the star, the moon, and the sun; namely, their appearing (al-zuhur) at one time and their disappearing (al-uful) at another. So appearing and disappearing are analogous to motion (al-haraka) and rest (al-sukun). So it is said in the inference on the origination of those celestial bodies by appearing and disappearing: If any of them had existed in preeternity (al-azal), it would not be free from either being apparent or being non-apparent. And the correlation (al-mulazama) is evident, since there is no intermediary between appearing and disappearing. And for that celestial body to be apparent in preeternity is impossible, for otherwise it would entail that it remain apparent forever;
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the fourth point, which establishes that the proof of the world's origination (huduth al-'alam) is derived from the Qur'anic narrative of Abraham's argument. The author states that the proof he has been following is taken from the proof that the Qur'an narrates from Abraham, peace be upon him. Specifically, Abraham inferred the origination of the star, moon, and sun from their appearing (zuhur) at one time and disappearing (uful) at another. The author explains that appearing and disappearing are analogous to motion (haraka) and rest (sukun). Then he begins to formulate the inference: if any of these celestial bodies existed in preeternity (al-azal), it would have to be either apparent or non-apparent (there being no middle state). The possibility of it being apparent in preeternity is impossible, because that would necessitate that it remain apparent forever, which is contradicted by the observation that it disappears. The text cuts off here, but the intended conclusion is that therefore none of these bodies existed in preeternity, so they are originated. This is the essence of Abraham's proof.

Correction: The author shows it is a valid rational argument analogous to the proof from motion and rest, grounded in observable alternation.

Checkpoint

B) light and darkness
C) existence and nonexistence
D) knowledge and ignorance

Key Takeaway
The proof of the world's origination is not only rational but also scriptural, as shown by Abraham's argument from appearance and disappearance.

?

Will you begin to look for logical arguments in the verses you recite? What would it take for you to engage with the Qur'an not only with your heart but also with your mind?
