Proof from the Perfection of the Shari'ah
Second supplementary proof for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the comprehensive wisdom of the Prophet's law (shari'ah) demonstrates that it is from God and he is a prophet.

Core Idea
A law with such profound wisdom cannot be from human invention.

The second proof examines the content of the shari'ah itself—its teachings on beliefs, worship, transactions, politics, and etiquette. Sanusi argues that the subtle wisdoms within demand that it must be divine revelation. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the second proof. Note the domains of shari'ah listed.
2
Identify the argument's structure
The proof states: whoever examines the shari'ah and sees its subtle wisdoms will know it is divine. Focus on the phrase 'علم قطعاً' (know with certainty).
3
Reflect on the implied premise
Think about why a human could not produce such a law. The wisdom and comprehensiveness point to a divine source.
This proof relies on the internal evidence of the law.
4
Connect to prophethood
The conclusion is that the bearer of such a law must be a prophet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالذي يُطْمَعُ في استقصائِهِ ، وهو ممَّا لا يمكنُ أنْ يُعَدَّ ولا يُحصى ولو أُفرِدَتْ له دواوين وأسفار كثيرةٌ
هذا الذي ذكرته هو العمدة المشهورة في إثباتِ النبوَّة ، وإلزام الحُجَّةِ على المعاندِ والمجادل .
وقد يُستدَلُّ بوجومٍ أُخَرَ ؛ تأكيداً لاطمئنان القلبِ ، ومبالغةً لدفعِ الوسواس وخطراتِ الريب :
الأولُ : أَنَّهُ قدِ اجتمعَ فيهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ مِنَ الأخلاقِ الحميدة ، والأوصافِ الشريفةِ ، والسِّيَرِ المرضيَّةِ ، والكمالاتِ العلميَّةِ والعمليّة ، والمحاسنِ الراجعة إلى النفس والبدن والنسب والوطن.. ما يجزمُ العقلُ بأنَّهُ لا يجتمع ذلك كلُّه إلا لنبي وتفاصيل ذلك لا يقوم بها إلا تصنيف مستقل
الثاني : أَنَّ مَنْ نظرَ فيما اشتملَتْ عليه شريعتهُ ممَّا يتعلَّقُ بالاعتقادات والعبادات والمعاملاتِ والسياسات والآداب ، وعلم ما فيها من دقائقِ الحِكَم . . علم قطعاً أنها ليست إلا وضعاً إلهياً ووحياً سماويّاً ، وأنَّ المبعوث بها ليس إلا نبياً .
الثالثُ : أَنَّهُ انتصبَ مَعَ ضعفِهِ ، وقلَّةِ ذاتِ يدِهِ ، وعدمِ آبائِهِ ، وقلة أعوانِهِ وأنصارِهِ.. حرباً لأهلِ الأَرضِ ، ذَاتِ الطُّولِ [؟]الملكِ في[؟] وقوَّةِ [؟]والعَرْضِ[؟] ، بأجمعهم ؛ آحادهم وأوساطهم ، وأكاسرتهم وجبابرتهم ؛ فضلَّل آراءَهم ، وسفّة أحلامهم ، وأبطل ملكهم ، وهدم دُولَهم ، وظهر دينُهُ على جميعِ الأديان ، وزاد على مر الأعصارِ والأزمان ، وانتشر في الآفاقِ والأقطار ، وشاع في المشارقِ والمغاربِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يقدرَ الأعداء مع كثرة عَدَدِهم وعُدَدِهم ، وشدَّةِ شوكتهم ، وحدَّةِ شكيمتِهم ، وفَرْطِ حميَّتِهم وعصبيَّتهم ، وبذلهم غاية الوسع في إطفاء أنواره ، وطمس آثارِهِ . . على إخمادِ شرارةٍ مِنْ نارِهِ ، فهل يكون ذلك إلا بعون إلهي ، وتأييد سماوي ؟!
وَلَيْسَ لِمَا تَبْنِي يَدُ اللَّهِ هَادِمُ
الرابع : أنَّهُ ظهر في زمانٍ أحوج ما كانَ الناسُ فِيهِ إِلَى مَنْ يهدي إلى الطريق المستقيم ، ويدعو إلى الدين القويم ، وينظم الأمور ، ويضبط حالَ الجمهورِ ؛ لكونه زمانَ فترةٍ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ، وتفرُّقِ السُّبُلِ
That which one aspires to exhaust completely, and it is something that cannot be counted or enumerated even if many books and volumes were devoted to it. This which I have mentioned is the famous foundation in proving prophethood, and compelling the argument against the obstinate and the disputant. And other proofs may also be adduced, to reinforce the heart's certainty and to maximize the repulsion of whisperings and thoughts of doubt: First: That there gathered in him (peace and blessings be upon him) noble morals, honorable qualities, pleasing conduct, intellectual and practical perfections, and excellences pertaining to the soul, body, lineage, and homeland... such that the mind decisively concludes that all of that gathers only in a prophet, and the details of that cannot be covered except by an independent treatise. Second: That whoever considers what his law contains regarding beliefs, acts of worship, transactions, politics, and etiquette, and knows the subtle wisdoms therein, will know with certainty that it is nothing other than a divine ordainment and a heavenly revelation, and that the one sent with it is nothing but a prophet. Third: That he rose up, despite his weakness, his lack of means, his lack of forefathers, and the scarcity of his helpers and supporters, as a war against all the people of the earth, those of extensive dominion, power, and breadth, all of them—their individuals, their middle classes, their Kisras, and their tyrants. He declared their opinions false, deemed their dreams foolish, invalidated their kingship, demolished their states, and his religion prevailed over all religions, increased over the ages and times, spread in the horizons and regions, and became common in the East and the West, while the enemies—despite their great numbers and equipment, their intense power, sharpness of their resolve, extreme zeal and partisanship, and their utmost effort to extinguish its lights and obliterate its traces—were unable to suppress a single spark of its fire. Is that then except through divine assistance and heavenly support? And there is no destroyer for what God's hand builds. Fourth: That he appeared at a time when people were most in need of someone to guide to the straight path, call to the upright religion, organize affairs, and control the public situation, because it was a time of interval between messengers and of division of paths.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage enumerates four supplementary rational proofs for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him), following the primary proof (referred to as 'al-umdah al-mashhurah'). The author introduces these additional proofs (wujud ukhara) as serving to reinforce the heart's certainty and to fully dispel whispers of doubt. The first proof (al-awwal) argues from the perfection of the Prophet's character, intellect, and personal qualities—such noble morals, virtues, and perfections in soul, body, lineage, and homeland—that the mind judges such a combination can only belong to a prophet. The second proof (al-thani) examines the content of his law (shari'ah), noting its comprehensive wisdom covering beliefs, worship, transactions, politics, and etiquette, concluding that such a system must be divine revelation and its bearer a prophet. The third proof (al-thalith) is a historical argument: despite the Prophet's initial weakness, lack of resources, and few supporters, he successfully waged war against the great empires of his time, eventually prevailing, and his religion spread widely. The enemies could not extinguish his message, which clearly indicates divine support (ta'yid samawi). The author ends this proof with a poetic line emphasizing that what God builds cannot be destroyed. The fourth proof (al-rabi') points to the timing of his mission: he appeared in an era of need—a period of interval (fatrah) between prophets, when people were lost and divided—making his appearance divinely timed. The passage thus provides a cumulative rational case for prophethood based on character, law, historical success, and timing.

Key Terms
الشريعة
دقائق الحكم
وضع إلهي
وحي سماوي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the Prophet authored the Quran and shari'ah himself.
Correction: The profound wisdom and comprehensiveness of the shari'ah demonstrate it is beyond human capacity, thus from God.

Checkpoint
What does the second proof rely on to conclude the shari'ah is from God?
A) The miracles of the Prophet
B) The subtle wisdoms in its teachings
C) The number of followers
D) The length of the Prophet's life

Key Takeaway
The profound wisdom of the shari'ah proves it is divine and its bearer a prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just encountered a proof that the shari'ah is divine because of its profound wisdom. If you truly believe this, what does it mean for the way you obey its commands? Is there any area of your life where you treat God's law as less important than your own desires? Will you commit today to investigating that area and submitting fully to His wisdom?
?
The passage lists five domains: beliefs, worship, transactions, politics, and etiquette. Which of these domains do you most often neglect or rationalize away from Islamic guidance? If you are convinced that the shari'ah covers all of life with divine wisdom, what step will you take this week to bring that area into alignment with the teaching of the Prophet?
?
The argument assumes that you have considered the subtle wisdoms of the shari'ah. Have you ever really pondered the wisdom behind a specific ruling? If not, what is stopping you? How would your faith be strengthened if you personally experienced the depth of God's wisdom in His law? Ask Allah to open your heart to the wonders of His shari'ah.

Prophethood
beginner

Proof from Historical Success
Third supplementary proof for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's extraordinary success against overwhelming odds demonstrates divine support, proving his prophethood.

Core Idea
One man, with no resources, defeated the world's empires—only God could have done this.

The third proof is a powerful historical argument: despite the Prophet's initial weakness and lack of supporters, he waged war against the great powers of his time, prevailed, and his religion spread globally. His enemies could not extinguish his message. This lesson analyzes how this outcome indicates divine aid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the third proof. Notice the stark contrast between the Prophet's weakness and the enemies' power.
2
Identify the elements of the argument
List: Prophet's condition (weakness, lack of means), opponents (all people, kings, empires), outcome (religion prevailed, spread), enemies' inability to stop it.
3
Understand the rhetorical question
The author asks: 'Is that except through divine assistance and heavenly support?' This is the key conclusion.
4
Appreciate the poetic closure
The line 'And there is no destroyer for what God's hand builds' reinforces the permanence of the Prophet's mission.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet's success was due to political maneuvering or luck.

A) They failed to kill the Prophet

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Prophet succeeded despite having no worldly power, do you truly believe that his success came from God alone? Or have you, in your heart, attributed his achievements to his own intelligence, strategy, or luck? Examine your faith: do you rely on God's support as the only source of victory in your life?
?
The enemies tried their utmost to extinguish the light of Islam but failed. What 'enemies' in your own life—such as persistent sin, doubts, or worldly distractions—are you tolerating as if they can overpower God's light within you? Are you fighting them with the same conviction that God will support you?
?
If the Prophet's success was a clear sign of divine assistance, why do you often doubt God's help in your own struggles? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that nothing can overcome what God builds?

Proof from Timing and Need
Fourth supplementary proof for prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's appearance at a time of spiritual need and division provides a rational proof for his prophethood.

Core Idea
He came exactly when humanity needed guidance the most.

The fourth proof considers the historical context: the interval between prophets (fatrah) when people had strayed into division and confusion. The Prophet appeared to guide them to the straight path and organize their affairs. This lesson shows why this timing is a sign of divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the fourth proof. Note the description of the time before the Prophet.
2
Identify the needs of the people
The passage mentions: need for guidance to straight path, call to upright religion, organization of affairs, and control of public situation.
3
Understand the context: fatrah
It was a period of interval between messengers and division of paths. This made the need urgent.
4
Connect timing to prophethood
The Prophet's appearance precisely at such a time indicates divine planning and confirms his prophetic mission.

الثالثُ : أَنَّهُ انتصبَ مَعَ ضعفِهِ ، وقلَّةِ ذاتِ يدِهِ ، وعدمِ آبائِهِ ، وقلة أعوانِهِ وأنصارِهِ.. حرباً لأهلِ الأَرضِ ، ذَاتِ الطُّولِ [؟]الملكِ في[؟] وقوَّةِ [؟]والعَرْضِ[؟] ، بأجمعهم ؛ آحادهم وأوساطهم ، وأكاسرتهم وجبابرتهم ؛ فضلَّل آراءَهم ، وسفّة أحلامهم ، وأبطل ملكهم ، وهدم دُولَهم ، وظهر دينُهُ على جميعِ الأديان ، وزاد على مر الأعصارِ والأزمان ، وانتشر في الآفاقِ والأقطار ، وشاع في المشارقِ والمغاربِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يقدرَ الأعداء مع كثرة عَدَدِهم وعُدَدِهم ، وشدَّةِ شوكتهم ، وحدَّةِ شكيمتِهم ، وفَرْطِ حميَّتِهم وعصبيَّتهم ، وبذلهم غاية الوسع في إطفاء أنواره ، وطمس آثارِهِ . . على إخمادِ شرارةٍ مِنْ نارِهِ ، فهل يكون ذلك إلا بعون إلهي ، وتأييد سماوي ؟!
وَلَيْسَ لِمَا تَبْنِي يَدُ اللَّهِ هَادِمُ
الرابع : أنَّهُ ظهر في زمانٍ أحوج ما كانَ الناسُ فِيهِ إِلَى مَنْ يهدي إلى الطريق المستقيم ، ويدعو إلى الدين القويم ، وينظم الأمور ، ويضبط حالَ الجمهورِ ؛ لكونه زمانَ فترةٍ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ، وتفرُّقِ السُّبُلِ
That which one aspires to exhaust completely, and it is something that cannot be counted or enumerated even if many books and volumes were devoted to it. This which I have mentioned is the famous foundation in proving prophethood, and compelling the argument against the obstinate and the disputant. And other proofs may also be adduced, to reinforce the heart's certainty and to maximize the repulsion of whisperings and thoughts of doubt: First: That there gathered in him (peace and blessings be upon him) noble morals, honorable qualities, pleasing conduct, intellectual and practical perfections, and excellences pertaining to the soul, body, lineage, and homeland... such that the mind decisively concludes that all of that gathers only in a prophet, and the details of that cannot be covered except by an independent treatise. Second: That whoever considers what his law contains regarding beliefs, acts of worship, transactions, politics, and etiquette, and knows the subtle wisdoms therein, will know with certainty that it is nothing other than a divine ordainment and a heavenly revelation, and that the one sent with it is nothing but a prophet. Third: That he rose up, despite his weakness, his lack of means, his lack of forefathers, and the scarcity of his helpers and supporters, as a war against all the people of the earth, those of extensive dominion, power, and breadth, all of them—their individuals, their middle classes, their Kisras, and their tyrants. He declared their opinions false, deemed their dreams foolish, invalidated their kingship, demolished their states, and his religion prevailed over all religions, increased over the ages and times, spread in the horizons and regions, and became common in the East and the West, while the enemies—despite their great numbers and equipment, their intense power, sharpness of their resolve, extreme zeal and partisanship, and their utmost effort to extinguish its lights and obliterate its traces—were unable to suppress a single spark of its fire. Is that then except through divine assistance and heavenly support? And there is no destroyer for what God's hand builds. Fourth: That he appeared at a time when people were most in need of someone to guide to the straight path, call to the upright religion, organize affairs, and control the public situation, because it was a time of interval between messengers and of division of paths.
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage enumerates four supplementary rational proofs for the prophethood of Muhammad (peace be upon him), following the primary proof (referred to as 'al-umdah al-mashhurah'). The author introduces these additional proofs (wujud ukhara) as serving to reinforce the heart's certainty and to fully dispel whispers of doubt. The first proof (al-awwal) argues from the perfection of the Prophet's character, intellect, and personal qualities—such noble morals, virtues, and perfections in soul, body, lineage, and homeland—that the mind judges such a combination can only belong to a prophet. The second proof (al-thani) examines the content of his law (shari'ah), noting its comprehensive wisdom covering beliefs, worship, transactions, politics, and etiquette, concluding that such a system must be divine revelation and its bearer a prophet. The third proof (al-thalith) is a historical argument: despite the Prophet's initial weakness, lack of resources, and few supporters, he successfully waged war against the great empires of his time, eventually prevailing, and his religion spread widely. The enemies could not extinguish his message, which clearly indicates divine support (ta'yid samawi). The author ends this proof with a poetic line emphasizing that what God builds cannot be destroyed. The fourth proof (al-rabi') points to the timing of his mission: he appeared in an era of need—a period of interval (fatrah) between prophets, when people were lost and divided—making his appearance divinely timed. The passage thus provides a cumulative rational case for prophethood based on character, law, historical success, and timing.

Key Terms
فترة الرسل
تفرق السبل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Prophet emerged at a random time in history.
Correction: The proof shows his appearance was at the most needed time, indicating divine planning.

Checkpoint
What was the condition of people before the Prophet according to the fourth proof?
A) They were united and prosperous
B) They were in need of guidance and divided
C) They had many prophets
D) They were peaceful

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's appearance at a time of spiritual crisis and division is a sign that his mission was divinely appointed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were living in that time of division and darkness, would you have truly felt the desperate need for a guide? Or would you have been content with the confusion?
?
The Prophet came to organize affairs and control the public situation. Is your own life organized according to his guidance, or is it still in chaos? What one step can you take today to submit more fully to his leadership?
?
You believe in the Prophet, but do you live as if his arrival was the most critical event in history? When you feel lost, do you turn to him or to the divided paths of this world?

The Third Proof: Victory Despite Weakness
Sanusi enumerates the Prophet's weaknesses and enemies' strengths to argue for divine support.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's overwhelming success despite his initial weakness serves as a clear proof of prophethood and divine support.

Core Idea
The Prophet's victory over the world while weak proves his prophethood is from Allah.

Sanusi now presents the third and most dramatic proof of prophethood: the Prophet Muhammad's unprecedented triumph against all odds. Despite being alone, poor, and without support, he challenged the entire world and prevailed. This passage invites us to reflect on the sheer impossibility of such success without divine aid.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the rhythmic language and the powerful conclusion.
The passage uses a rhetorical question to drive home the point.
2
Identify the Prophet's disadvantages
List all the weaknesses mentioned: his personal weakness, scarcity of resources, lack of lineage, and few supporters.
These are deliberately contrasted with the enemies' strength.
3
Identify the scale of opposition
Notice how Sanusi describes the enemies: all people of the earth, from commoners to kings, with numbers, equipment, and zeal.
The description emphasizes the impossibility of victory without divine aid.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
After listing the Prophet's victories and the enemies' inability to stop him, Sanusi asks: this can only be through divine assistance. Internalize this as a proof of prophethood.
The final poetic line reinforces that Allah's support cannot be undone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : أَنَّهُ انتصبَ مَعَ ضعفِهِ ، وقلَّةِ ذاتِ يدِهِ ، وعدمِ آبائِهِ ، وقلة أعوانِهِ وأنصارِهِ.. حرباً لأهلِ الأَرضِ ، ذاتِ الطُّولِ والعَرْضِ ، بأجمعهم ؛ آحادهم وأوساطهم ، وأكاسرتهم وجبابرتهم ؛ فضلَّل آراءَهم ، وسفَّة أحلامهم ، وأبطل ملكهم ، وهدم دُولَهم ، وظهر دينُهُ على جميعِ الأديان ، وزاد على مر الأعصارِ والأزمان ، وانتشر في الآفاقِ والأقطار ، وشاع في المشارقِ والمغاربِ ، مِنْ غيرِ أنْ يقدرَ الأعداء مع كثرة عَدَدِهِم وعُدَدِهِم ، وشدَّةِ شوكتهم ، وحدَّةِ شكيمتِهم ، وفَرْطِ حميَّتِهم وعصبيَّتهم ، وبذلهم غاية الوسع في إطفاء أنواره ، وطمس آثارِهِ . . على إخمادِ شرارةٍ مِنْ نارِهِ ، فهل يكون ذلك إلا بعون إلهي ، وتأييد سماوي ؟! وَلَيْسَ لِمَا تَبْنِي يَدُ اللَّهِ هَادِمُ
The third: that he (the Prophet) stood up, despite his weakness, scarcity of resources, lack of supporters, and few helpers and allies, in war against the people of the earth, of length and breadth, all of them: their individuals and middle classes, their kings and tyrants. He deemed their opinions foolish, their intellects deficient, nullified their kingdom, demolished their states, and his religion prevailed over all religions, increased over the course of centuries and times, spread in the horizons and regions, and became widespread in the East and West, without the enemies, despite their great numbers and equipment, the intensity of their power, the sharpness of their resolve, the excess of their zeal and partisanship, and their utmost effort in extinguishing his lights and obliterating his traces, being able to put out a spark of his fire. Would that be except with divine assistance and heavenly support? And there is no destroyer for what the hand of Allah builds.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof of prophethood: the overwhelming success of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ despite his initial weakness and lack of material support. Sanusi lists the Prophet's disadvantages (weakness, few resources, no lineage, few supporters) and then describes how he waged war against all the people of the earth, from commoners to kings. He defeated their ideas, abolished their kingdoms, and his religion spread everywhere. Despite the enemies' immense power and efforts to extinguish his light, they could not even put out a spark. Sanusi concludes with a rhetorical question: this can only be through divine aid. The poetic line reinforces that what Allah builds cannot be destroyed.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's success was due to political or military strategy alone.
Correction: This proof shows that his victory was beyond human capacity, as he was weak and outnumbered, yet he prevailed against all enemies.

The Prophet's triumph against overwhelming odds is a clear sign that his mission was supported by Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The enemies used every effort to extinguish the Prophet's light, yet they failed. Have you ever been embarrassed or hesitant to share Islam because it seemed weak today? Reflect on the contrast with the Prophet's confidence despite his weakness. What is one step you can take to show reliance on Allah's support?
?
The phrase 'there is no destroyer for what the hand of Allah builds' is a promise. Is there something in your life that you fear will be destroyed? Do you truly believe that if Allah builds it, it cannot be ruined? What would change in your attitude if you embraced this certainty?

The Fourth Proof: Prophet's Appearance Amidst Universal Corruption
Sanusi enumerates the corruption of seven nations and concludes all were in misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's appearance at a time of maximal human need and moral decay serves as a proof of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet came when humanity needed guidance most, proving his mission was divine.

Sanusi presents the fourth proof of prophethood: the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ appeared at a time when humanity was engulfed in corruption, misguidance, and moral decay. By detailing the state of various nations—Arabs, Persians, Turks, Indians, Jews, Christians, and others—Sanusi shows that the world was in desperate need of divine guidance. This lesson explores the condition of each civilization, demonstrating the necessity and wisdom of the Prophet's mission.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the first part of the Arabic passage where Sanusi states the fourth proof: the Prophet appeared at the most needy time.
Notice the phrase 'أحوج ما كان الناس' meaning 'most in need'.
2
Examine each nation's condition
Go through the description of each nation: Arabs, Persians, Turks, Indians, Jews, Christians, and others. Note the specific corruptions mentioned.
The passage uses vivid language to emphasize their misguidance.
3
Reflect on the timing
Ask yourself why this period—'zaman al-fatrah' (interval between prophets)—was the most suitable for sending the final Prophet.
Compare with the need for guidance.
4
Connect to the proof
Understand how the universal corruption proves that the Prophet could not have invented his message; only divine intervention could rescue humanity.
5
Summarize the argument
Write a short summary of how this passage serves as evidence for prophethood.
You can use the key_takeaway as a guide.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : أنَّهُ ظهر في زمانٍ أحوج ما كانَ الناسُ فِيهِ إِلَى مَنْ يهدي إلى الطريق المستقيم ، ويدعو إلى الدين القويم ، وينظم الأمور ، ويضبط حالَ الجمهورِ ؛ لكونه زمانَ فترةٍ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ ، وتفرُّقِ السُّبُلِ ، وانحراف في المِلَلِ ، واختلافِ للدول ، واشتعال للضلال ، واشتغال بالمحال . فالعرب على بكرة أبيها عاكفة على عبادة الأوثان ، ووأد البنات وادعاء كثيرٍ منهم أنَّ الملائكة بنات اللهِ عزَّ وجلَّ ! والفُرْسُ معَ كثرتها كثرة الحصى دائمة على إيقاد النيران ، واتخاذها آلهة مِن دونِ الرحمن ، وإباحتها رذيلة وطء الأُمَّهاتِ وتحليلها نكاح الإخوة والأخوات ! والأتراكُ جاهدَتْ جهدَها في تخريب البلادِ ، وتعذيب العباد ! والهند جاثمة على عبادةِ البقر ، والسجود للحجر والشجرِ واليهود قد أُولعَتْ بالجحودِ وإخماد الحقِّ ، وتمسَّكَتْ بقول الباطل ، واعتقادِ الجسمية والصورة ونحوهما لَمَنْ تنزّه عن النقائص وسماتِ الخلْقِ ، وتديَّنَتْ بالغشّ حتى في تبديل الدين والشرائع وصفاتِ الرُّسُلِ التي كانَتْ محفوظةً عندَها في الألواحِ والوَرَقِ . والنصارى أصبحت حيارى سكارى ، في خبط عظيم وتناقض يلعب فيه بعقولها الشيطان الرجيم ، حتى تجرَّأَتْ ونسبتِ الولد للمولى الذي جلَّ أنْ يكونَ والداً أو مولوداً ، وثلَّثَتِ الإله ، وفاهَتْ بهذيان لا يرضى به ذو عقل ، وأمسَتْ لغيرِ مولانا جل وعزَّ رُكَّعاً وسجوداً ، وصارَ مَنْ لم يصلح للألوهية ألبتة إلهاً عندها معبوداً . وهكذا سائرُ الفِرَقِ ، كلُّ يخوضُ في أودية الضلال
The fourth: that he appeared at a time when people were most in need of someone to guide to the straight path, call to the upright religion, organize affairs, and manage the state of the masses; because it was a time of interval between messengers, divergence of paths, deviation in creeds, conflict of states, kindling of misguidance, and engagement with falsehood. The Arabs, all of them, were devoted to idol worship, burying daughters, and many of them claiming that the angels are daughters of Allah Almighty! The Persians, with their number like pebbles, were constantly kindling fires, taking them as deities besides the Most Merciful, and permitting the abomination of incest with mothers and making lawful the marriage of brothers and sisters! The Turks strove their utmost in destroying lands and torturing servants! The Indians were crouched on worshipping the cow, prostrating to stone and tree. The Jews were obsessed with denial, extinguishing truth, clinging to false statements, belief in corporeality and form and the like for Him who is transcendent above deficiencies and attributes of creation, and they practiced deceit even in altering religion, laws, and descriptions of messengers which were preserved with them in tablets and paper. The Christians became bewildered, drunk, in great confusion and contradiction in which the accursed Satan played with their minds, until they dared to attribute a son to the Master who is far above being a father or born, trinitized God, and uttered nonsense with which no intelligent person would be satisfied, and they became bowing and prostrating to other than our Master, Mighty and Sublime, and one who is absolutely not fit for divinity became for them a worshipped god. And likewise the rest of the sects, each plunging into valleys of misguidance.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof of prophethood: the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ came at a time of maximum corruption and deviation, when humanity desperately needed guidance. Sanusi describes the time as a period of interval between prophets, with conflicting paths, corrupted creeds, and widespread misguidance. He then details the state of various nations: Arabs engaged in idolatry, infanticide, and slander; Persians worshipping fire and practicing incest; Turks destroying and torturing; Indians worshipping cows and stones; Jews distorting scriptures and attributing physical form to God; Christians falling into trinitarian polytheism and idol worship. All were in deep misguidance. This context highlights the necessity of the Prophet's mission and the divine wisdom in sending him precisely then.

Key Terms
زمان الفترة
أدلة النبوة
الضلال
الجاهلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Prophet appeared in an advanced civilization.
Correction: Sanusi shows the moral and religious decay of all major civilizations at that time.

Checkpoint

C) Because the previous prophets had failed.
D) Because there were no other religions.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's appearance at the height of corruption underscores the divine origin of his message, as human constructs could not have produced such guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you feel surrounded by confusion and falsehood (social media, peer pressure, mainstream culture), do you instinctively turn to the sunnah as your anchor, or do you drift with the current? What is one specific habit you can change this week to align more with the Prophet's way?
?
The Prophet came at a time when all nations were in ‘valleys of misguidance.’ If you were to examine your own heart and actions honestly, do you find any ‘valley’ where you are following the ways of those nations—like the Arabs’ attachment to status, the Persians’ pleasure-seeking, or the Christians’ compromise on tawhid? What will you do to climb out?

The Necessity of Muhammad's Mission
Sanusi describes the corruption of mankind and God's sending of Muhammad as the renewer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses the concept of God's custom (ʿādat Allāh) and the evident corruption of the world to argue for the necessity of Muhammad's prophethood.

Core Idea
God's custom is to send a renewer when corruption peaks; Muhammad is that renewer.

Sanusi now builds a powerful argument for the necessity of Muhammad's mission. He first describes the universal corruption that had overtaken humanity, then presents God's established pattern of sending a reformer when things are at their worst. The passage culminates in the assertion that Muhammad alone fits this description, a fact he claims is known necessarily.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Let the rhetorical flow sink in.
Notice the dramatic opening describing corruption.
2
Identify the description of corruption
Find the phrases that describe the extent of error and disorder. What words are used?
Key terms: ضلال, خبط, تخليط, فساد.
3
Find the statement of God's custom
Locate the sentence beginning with 'قد أُلِفَ مِنْ عادة مولانا...' What does it say about God's pattern?
The custom is to send a renewer when corruption is extreme.
4
Note the claim of necessary knowledge
Read the sentence 'ومن المعلوم ضرورة...' and note what is claimed to be known necessarily.
It asserts that no one but Muhammad rebuilt the ruined structure.
5
Reflect on the effects of Muhammad's mission
List the outcomes of his mission mentioned in the passage. How do they confirm the argument?
Effects include mending corruption, distinguishing truth, spreading knowledge, etc.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا عرفت هذا الضلال والخبط والتخليط الذي كان في الخَلْقِ ، وتناهى فيهم وكمل ، وعم الأمصار والقرى ، والبر والبحر ، والسهل والجبل . . فنقولُ :
قد أُلِفَ مِنْ عادة مولانا جل وعزَّ أنَّ عباده إذا بلغوا هذا المبلغ في
الفسادِ المتناهي المبين .. بعثَ إليهم بمحْضِ فضلِهِ مَنْ يُجدِّدُ لهم ما عمي عنهم مِنْ أمور الدين (۱) ، ويرسلُ حينئذ الرُّسُلَ رحمة للعالمينَ ؛ كما قالَ جلَّ مِنْ قائل : ﴿ كَانَ النَّاسُ أُمَّةً وَاحِدَةً فَبَعَثَ اللَّهُ النَّبِيِّنَ مُبَشِّرِينَ وَمُنذِرِينَ ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۱۳] .
ومن المعلوم ضرورةً : أنَّه لم يظهر أحدٌ أَسَّسَ اللهُ تعالى بهِ مُنْهِدِمَ هذا البنيان سوى سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، أفيليقُ أن يختلف بعد في رسالتِهِ اثنانِ ؟! فهو الذي أصلحَ الله تعالى بهِ ما فسدَ مِنْ شأن الناس ، وميَّزَ بهِ الحقَّ مِنَ الباطل ، وأنشأ به دينَ اللهِ تعالى على أمتنِ أساس ، وانجلى بهِ عن القلوب ظلماتها ، وأُنقِذَتْ بهِ مِنْ لُجَحِ الفساد ، وطلعتْ عليها شموس المعارفِ ، وانتشرَتْ ببركة أنواره في البلاد والعبادِ ، وارتجّتِ الأرضُ بذكرِ اللهِ تعالى حقَّ ذكرِهِ ، وظهرَ سفهُ مَنْ أسند على الحقيقة أثراً مِنَ الآثارِ إلى غيرِهِ ، وارتفعَتْ
بتحميدِهِ جلَّ وعزَّ وتمجيدِهِ وتوحيدِهِ وتقديسه عن سماتِ الحدوثِ والافتقار .. الأصواتُ في المساجد والصوامع والمنابر ، ونبعَتْ ينابيع الحِكَمِ الجمَّةِ والمعارفِ النورانيَّةِ ، وفاضَتْ على القلوب والألسنة ؛ امتلاً ببعضها ما لا يُحاط بهِ ولا يُحصى مِنْ عددِ الأوراقِ حتى والدفاتر
فلمولانا جل وعلا الحمدُ على نِعَم عجز عن إحصاء القليل منها الأوائل والأواخرُ ، وعلى نبيَّهِ الذي أنعم به علينا بمحْض فضلِهِ ؛ سيدنا ومولانا محمدٍ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أفضل الصلواتِ وأكمل التحياتِ ، ما استمدَّتْ لإشادة محاسنِهِ ، وإفادة معارفِهِ . . الأقلامُ مِنَ
المحابر .
When you have recognized this error, confusion, and disorder that was among creation, reaching its peak and completion, and encompassing cities and villages, land and sea, plain and mountain... then we say: It has been the custom of our Master, Glorified and Exalted, that when His servants reach this degree of evident extreme corruption, He sends to them, by His sheer grace, one who renews for them what they have become blind to of the matters of religion (1), and He sends at that time the messengers as a mercy to the worlds; as He, Glorious in saying, said: {Mankind was one community; then Allah sent the prophets as bringers of good tidings and warners} [al-Baqarah 2:213]. And it is known necessarily that no one appeared through whom Allah, exalted be He, established the ruined structure except our Master and Lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Is it fitting that any two [people] should differ after this about his message? For it is he through whom Allah, exalted be He, mended what had become corrupt of the affairs of people, through whom He distinguished truth from falsehood, through whom He established the religion of Allah, exalted be He, on the firmest basis, through whom darknesses were removed from hearts, through whom [people] were rescued from the depths of corruption, upon whom the suns of knowledges rose, and by the blessing of his lights spread in lands and among servants, and the earth trembled with the remembrance of Allah, exalted be He, as He should be remembered, and the folly of those who attribute any effect from effects to other than the truth became apparent, and voices rose in the mosques, monasteries, and pulpits with praise of Him, Glorified and Exalted, and glorification of Him, and declaring His oneness, and declaring His transcendence above the characteristics of origination and need... and springs of abundant wisdoms and luminous knowledges gushed forth, and overflowed upon hearts and tongues; some of them filled what cannot be encompassed or counted of the number of papers and notebooks. So for our Master, Glorious and Exalted, is all praise for blessings whose number the first and last are incapable of enumerating even a small part of them, and for His Prophet through whom He favored us by His sheer grace; our Master and Lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the best of blessings and most complete salutations, as long as pens draw from inkwells to extol his virtues and convey his knowledges.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is a rhetorical argument for the necessity of Muhammad's prophethood. It begins by describing the universal corruption that had reached its peak, then states God's custom of sending a renewer or messenger when corruption is extreme. It then asserts as a matter of necessary knowledge that no one other than Muhammad fulfilled this role. The passage lists the effects of his mission: mending corruption, distinguishing truth, establishing religion firmly, removing darkness, rescuing people, spreading knowledge, etc. It concludes with praise to God for these blessings and invocation of blessings on the Prophet. The argument relies on the premise that the need for a reformer is evident and that Muhammad's unique impact is undeniable.

Key Terms
عادة الله
المعلوم ضرورة
النبوة
التجديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the passage argues from mere historical accident or subjective opinion.
Correction: The passage claims necessary knowledge (المعلوم ضرورة) that Muhammad alone fulfilled the role, based on the observable effects and God's custom.

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the claim that no one other than Muhammad could have been the promised renewer, according to this passage?
A) A direct revelation to the author
B) It is known necessarily from the state of the world and God's custom
C) The consensus of all scholars
D) The miraculous nature of the Quran

Key Takeaway
Sanusi argues that Muhammad's mission is necessary because God customarily sends a reformer when corruption peaks, and Muhammad alone fulfilled that role.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The corruption described once engulfed the entire world. But what about the corruption in your own soul—right now—that you have become accustomed to and no longer see? What would it mean for you to sincerely ask God, by His sheer grace, to send you a renewal before it is too late?
?
Sanusi says it is known necessarily that only Muhammad established the ruined structure. Do you live as if this is true? When was the last time you let the light of his message pierce a darkness you have been hiding in your heart? What would change if you truly submitted to his renewal tonight?
?
God sent Muhammad as a mercy to the worlds, and that mercy has reached you. But have you received it? Or have you kept it at arm's length, letting the noise of your own desires drown out the call? What would it cost you to finally let his renewal break through the walls you have built?

The Fifth Proof: Glad Tidings in Previous Scriptures
Sanusi introduces the fifth proof and cites a Torah passage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the fifth proof for Muhammad's prophethood is based on glad tidings in earlier scriptures, and you will see an example from the Torah.

Core Idea
Previous scriptures foretold Muhammad's coming – a key external proof.

Sanusi now introduces the fifth proof of Muhammad's prophethood: the glad tidings found in the books of earlier prophets. These texts, well-known among their nations, are numerous. He begins by citing a passage from the Torah, which Muslim scholars interpret as referring to the prophetic missions of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. This lesson presents the opening of this proof and its first example.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice how Sanusi introduces the fifth proof and begins quoting the Torah.
The quote is incomplete – it sets up the argument for the proof.
2
Identify the proof type
Understand that this proof relies on prior revelation – prophecies from earlier prophets – as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood.
This differs from proofs based on miracles or logical arguments.
3
Examine the Torah example
Look at the citation from the fifth book of the Torah (Deuteronomy). Consider how it might be interpreted as referring to Muhammad along with Moses and Jesus.
The full quote would continue, but this fragment shows the method.
4
Address a common misunderstanding
Some might think this proof requires direct naming, but it is based on interpreted signs. Reflect on why this is still considered strong evidence by scholars.
This is a key nuance in understanding the proof.

[ النصوص المقدَّسة المبشِّرةُ بنبينا وسيّدِنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ] الخامس مِنَ الأدلَّةِ الدالة على ثبوتِ نبوة سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ (۱) : النصوص الواردة في كُتُبِ المتقدمينَ مِنَ الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، المنقولة إلى القرى المشهورة فيما بينَ أممهم ، وهي نصوص كثيرة جداً ، نذكر بعضها :
أما في التوراة : فمنها : ما جاءَ في السفرِ الخامس منه : ( جاءَ اللهُ مِنْ طُورِ سيناءَ ، وأشرقَ مِنْ ساغيـنَ (٢) ، واستعلـنَ مِـنْ جبـال
[The Sacred Texts that Give Glad Tidings of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace] The fifth of the proofs indicating the establishment of the prophethood of our Master and Lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace (1): The texts transmitted in the books of the former prophets, peace be upon them, which are well-known among their nations; they are very many texts. We will mention some of them: As for the Torah: among them is what came in its fifth book: 'Allah came from Mount Sinai, and shone from Sa'ir (2), and appeared from the mountains...'
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage introduces the fifth proof for Muhammad's prophethood: the prophecies in previous scriptures. The author states that these texts are found in the books of earlier prophets and are well-known. He then begins to cite an example from the Torah, specifically from its fifth book (Deuteronomy), quoting a passage that speaks of God coming from Sinai and shining from Seir. This is traditionally interpreted by Muslim scholars as alluding to the prophetic missions of Moses, Jesus, and Muhammad. The quote is cut off, but it initiates this proof.

Key Terms

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof requires a direct, explicit mention of Muhammad by name in previous scriptures.
Correction: The proof works through signs and symbolic references interpreted by scholars, not necessarily explicit naming.

Key Takeaway
The glad tidings in previous scriptures constitute a valid proof of Muhammad's prophethood, beginning with a Torah passage interpreted as a prophecy.

Fifth Proof of Prophethood: Torah Prophecies
Sanusi presents the fifth proof of prophethood: prophecies from the Torah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses prophecies from the Torah as evidence for the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH).

Core Idea
Torah prophecies about a prophet from Ishmael's descendants point directly to Muhammad.

Sanusi now turns to the scriptures of previous prophets, specifically the Torah, to show that the coming of Muhammad was foretold. These prophecies, preserved and transmitted among the nations, serve as a powerful proof for his prophethood. In this lesson, we examine two key passages from Deuteronomy that Sanusi interprets as clear annunciations of our Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Read the introductory passage where Sanusi states that the fifth proof consists of texts from earlier scriptures. Note that he says there are many such texts.
This proof relies on the preservation and transmission of these texts.
2
Examine the first prophecy
Read the verse from Deuteronomy 33:2 about God coming from Sinai, Seir, and Paran. Understand Sanusi's interpretation: each location corresponds to a revelation.
Paran is identified as Mecca or its vicinity.
3
Examine the second prophecy
Read the verse from Deuteronomy 18:15-22 about a prophet raised from among the brethren of Israel. Understand how Sanusi identifies 'brethren' as the Children of Ishmael.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النصوص المقدسة المبشرة بنبينا وسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم
الخامس من الأدلة الدالة على ثبوت نبوة سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم: النصوص الواردة في كتب المتقدمين من الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، المنقولة إلى القرى المشهورة فيما بين أممهم، وهي نصوص كثيرة جدا، نذكر بعضها:
أما في التوراة: فمنها: ما جاء في السفر الخامس منه: (جاء الله من طور سيناء، وأشرق من ساغين، واستعلن من جبال فاران)، وذلك كناية عن إنزال التوراة على موسى عليه السلام بطور سيناء، والإنجيل على عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بساغين، وهو من جبال الشام، وإنزال الفرقان على سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم بفاران؛ فإن فاران هي مكة أو طريق قريب منها، فمعنى (جاء الله) أي: شرعه ودينه الحق. وانظر كيف عبر في التوراة عن ظهور نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم بالاستعلان؛ إشارة إلى كثرة معجزاته، وإظهار دينه على الدين كله، وانتشاره وبقائه إلى أن تقوم الساعة.
ومنها: ما جاء في السفر الخامس من أنه تعالى قال لموسى عليه الصلاة والسلام في التوراة: (إني مقيم لبني إسرائيل نبيا من بني إخوتهم مثلك، وأجري قولي في فيه، ويقول لهم ما آمرهم به، والرجل الذي لا يقبل قول النبي الذي يتكلم باسمي فأنا أنتقم منه)، والمراد ببني إخوة بني إسرائيل: بنو إسماعيل؛ إذ إسرائيل من ولد إسحاق أخي إسماعيل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، ولم يبعث من ولد إسماعيل بعد موسى عليهما الصلاة والسلام غير سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم.
The sacred annunciatory texts about our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. The fifth of the proofs indicating the establishment of the prophethood of our Master and Patron Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace: the texts found in the books of the earlier prophets, peace be upon them, transmitted to the well-known towns among their nations, and they are very numerous texts; we mention some of them: As for the Torah: among them is what came in the fifth book of it: 'God came from Mount Sinai, and shone forth from Seir, and manifested from the mountains of Paran.' This is a metaphor for the sending down of the Torah upon Moses, peace be upon him, on Mount Sinai; and the Gospel upon Jesus, peace be upon him, in Seir, which is from the mountains of Syria; and the sending down of the Criterion upon our Master and Patron Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, in Paran; for Paran is Mecca or a road near it. So the meaning of 'God came' is His law and His true religion. And see how He expressed in the Torah the appearance of our Prophet and Master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, with 'manifestation' as an indication of the abundance of his miracles, and the manifestation of his religion over all religion, and its spread and survival until the Hour is established. And among them is what came in the fifth book that God Almighty said to Moses, peace be upon him, in the Torah: 'I will raise up for the Children of Israel a prophet from among their brethren like you, and I will put My words in his mouth, and he will speak to them all that I command him. And the man who does not accept the words of the prophet who speaks in My name, I will take vengeance on him.' And what is meant by 'the brethren of the Children of Israel' is the Children of Ishmael; for Israel is from the descendants of Isaac, the brother of Ishmael, peace be upon them. And no one was sent from the Children of Ishmael after Moses, peace be upon them, other than our Master and Patron Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace.
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof of the prophethood of Muhammad (PBUH), which is the presence of prophecies about him in earlier scriptures, specifically the Torah. Sanusi begins by stating that these texts are numerous and widely transmitted among the nations. He then provides two examples from the fifth book of the Torah (Deuteronomy). The first example is a verse (Deut 33:2) that says God came from Sinai, shone from Seir, and manifested from Paran. Sanusi interprets this as a metaphor for the revelations given to three prophets: the Torah to Moses at Sinai, the Gospel to Jesus at Seir (a mountain in Syria), and the Quran (al-Furqan) to Muhammad at Paran, which he identifies as Mecca or its vicinity. The phrase 'God came' is understood to mean the coming of His law and religion. Sanusi then notes that the expression 'manifested' (ist'alana) in the Torah alludes to the abundant miracles of Muhammad and the eventual dominance and spread of his religion until the Day of Judgment. The second example (Deut 18:15-22) is a statement by God to Moses that He will raise up a prophet from among the 'brethren' of the Children of Israel, like Moses, and will put His words in that prophet's mouth. Sanusi explains that 'brethren of the Children of Israel' refers to the Children of Ishmael, since Isaac (father of Israel) and Ishmael were brothers. After Moses, no prophet from the Ishmaelites appeared except Muhammad, thereby fulfilling this prophecy. The argument is that these explicit scriptural predictions serve as evidence for Muhammad's prophethood, as they were preserved and acknowledged by the People of the Book.

Key Terms
النصوص المقدسة المبشرة
السفر الخامس
فاران
بني إخوة بني إسرائيل
الاستعلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These prophecies are allegorical and do not literally predict Muhammad.
Correction: Sanusi treats them as direct and clear annunciations, citing specific geographical and genealogical details to support literal fulfillment.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the term 'Paran' refer to in the Torah prophecy?
A) A mountain in Syria
B) Mecca or a road near it
C) Mount Sinai
D) The land of Canaan

Key Takeaway
The Torah contains clear prophecies about the coming of a prophet from the descendants of Ishmael, which Sanusi identifies as Muhammad.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear that your prophet was foretold in the Torah, does your heart feel a deeper certainty? What one thing will you do today to live in a way that honors that prophethood?
?
The Torah warns that God will take vengeance on those who reject the prophet spoken of. Have you ever considered the weight of that statement for your own belief? How can you ensure you are not among those who reject, even subtly?
?
If you truly believe that the global spread of Islam from Paran is a fulfilled prophecy, what does that demand from you personally in terms of spreading the message or embodying it? What step will you take this week to act on that belief?

Torah Prophecy from Faran
Sanusi interprets the Torah's mention of Faran as a prophecy of Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi interprets the biblical reference to Faran as a prophecy of Muhammad's prophethood and the spread of Islam.

Core Idea
A biblical phrase about Faran points to the coming of Muhammad.

This lesson examines a passage where Sanusi draws on the Torah to argue that the coming of Prophet Muhammad was foretold in earlier scriptures. He interprets the phrase 'God came from Faran' as a metaphor for the revelation of divine books, culminating with the Qur'an in Mecca. The passage also highlights the word 'shining forth' as a description of the Prophet's miracles and the enduring triumph of Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the reference to three scriptures.
2
Identify the three revelations
The passage mentions the revelation of the Torah, the Gospel, and the Furqan (Qur'an). Note the locations: Sinai, Saghin, and Faran.
Faran is identified as Mecca or its vicinity.
3
Understand the interpretation of 'God came'
Sanusi explains that 'God came' does not mean a literal movement but refers to the advent of His Sharia and true religion.
This avoids anthropomorphism.
4
Reflect on 'shining forth'
The Torah's use of 'shining forth' is highlighted as a sign of Muhammad's abundant miracles, the universal dominance of his religion, and its continuity until the Day of Judgment.
This underscores the uniqueness of Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاران) (۱)، وذلك كناية عن إنزال التوراة على موسى عليهِ السلامُ بطُورِ سيناء، والإنجيل على عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بساغينَ، وهو مِنْ جبال الشام، وإنزال الفرقانِ على سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بفارانَ؛ فإنَّ فاران هي مكة أو طريق قريب منها، فمعنى ( جاءَ الله ) أي: شرعُهُ ودينه الحق. وانظر كيف عبَّرَ في التوراة عن ظهورِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بالاستعلانِ؛ إشارةً إلى كثرة معجزاته، وإظهار دينه على الدين كله، وانتشارِهِ وبقائِهِ إلى أن تقوم الساعةُ.
Faran (1): that is a metaphor for the revelation of the Torah to Moses (peace be upon him) at Mount Sinai, and the Gospel to Jesus (peace and blessings be upon him) at Saghin, which is from the mountains of al-Sham, and the revelation of the Furqan to our master and lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) at Faran; for Faran is Mecca or a nearby road. So the meaning of 'Allah came' is: His Sharia and His true religion. And see how the Torah expressed the advent of our prophet and lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) with 'shining forth', indicating the abundance of his miracles, the manifestation of his religion over all religions, its spread and continuity until the Hour is established.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage presents a prophetic proof from the Torah. It begins by explaining that the term 'Faran' is a metaphor for the revelation of the Torah, Gospel, and Furqan (Qur'an). The author identifies Faran as Mecca or its vicinity, linking the biblical phrase 'God came from Faran' to the coming of Muhammad. He then interprets 'God came' to mean His Sharia and true religion, not a literal movement. The author then highlights the word 'shining forth' in the Torah as an indication of the abundant miracles of Muhammad, the universal triumph of his religion, and its persistence until the end of time. This argument uses scriptural reference to validate prophethood.

Key Terms
فاران
التوراة
الإنجيل
الفرقان
الاستعلان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'God came' in the Torah refers to a literal divine descent.
Correction: Sanusi explains that it is a metaphor for the advent of His Sharia and true religion, not a physical movement.

The Torah Prophecy of a Prophet Like Moses
Sanusi cites a Torah prophecy and identifies Muhammad as its fulfillment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses a biblical prophecy from Deuteronomy to prove that Muhammad is the promised prophet like Moses.

Core Idea
A prophecy in Deuteronomy points to Muhammad as the promised prophet like Moses.

This lesson examines one of the scriptural proofs Sanusi offers for Muhammad's prophethood: a prophecy from the Torah. The passage cites a verse from Deuteronomy where God promises to raise a prophet like Moses from among the 'brethren' of Israel. Sanusi then explains that 'brethren' refers to the Children of Ishmael, and that only Muhammad from that lineage fits the description. Understanding this argument helps us see how earlier scriptures foretold the coming of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice that it begins with a quotation from the Torah, then explains the key term 'brethren', and ends with the conclusion that Muhammad is that prophet.
The passage is concise—every phrase matters.
2
Identify the biblical verse
Find the exact wording of the prophecy in the passage. God says He will raise a prophet 'like Moses' from their brethren, put words in his mouth, and punish those who reject him.
3
Understand the interpretation
Sanusi clarifies that 'brethren of Israel' means the Children of Ishmael. He uses the family tree: Israel (Jacob) is descended from Isaac, brother of Ishmael. So the prophet must come from Ishmael's line.
This is the key step that links the prophecy to Muhammad.
4
Appreciate the conclusion
After Moses, no prophet came from Ishmael's descendants except Muhammad. Therefore, this prophecy is uniquely fulfilled by him. Consider how this strengthens the case for his prophethood.
This conclusion relies on the historical fact that Muhammad was the only prophet from Ishmael's line after Moses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها: ما جاءَ في السفرِ الخامس مِنْ أنّهُ تعالى قالَ لموسى عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلامُ في التوراة: ( إنّي مقيمٌ لبني إسرائيل نبياً مِنْ بني مثلكَ، وأجري قولي في فيه، ويقول لهم ما آمرهم به، والرجل الذي لا يقبلُ قول النبي الذي يتكلم باسمي فأنا أنتقم منه )، والمراد ببني إخوة بني إسرائيل: بنو إسماعيل؛ إذ إسرائيل من ولد إسحاق أخي إسماعيل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، ولم يُبْعَثْ مِنْ ولد إسماعيل بعد موسى عليهما الصلاةُ والسلام غيرُ سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ.
And among them: what came in the fifth book that He, the Exalted, said to Moses (peace and blessings be upon him) in the Torah: 'I will raise up for them a prophet from among their brethren, like you, and I will put my words in his mouth, and he shall speak to them all that I command him. And the man who does not heed the words of the prophet who speaks in my name, I will take vengeance on him.' And the meaning of 'the brethren of the Children of Israel' is the Children of Ishmael, for Israel is from the descendants of Isaac, the brother of Ishmael (peace be upon them), and no prophet has been sent from the descendants of Ishmael after Moses (peace be upon him) other than our master and lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace).
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is another scriptural proof from the book of Deuteronomy. The author quotes the verse where God promises to raise a prophet like Moses from among the 'brethren' of the Israelites. He then explains that 'brethren' refers to the Children of Ishmael because Israel (Jacob) is descended from Isaac, the brother of Ishmael. After Moses, the only prophet from Ishmael's line was Muhammad. The proof argues that this prophecy uniquely fits Muhammad, who resembles Moses in bringing a law and being a messenger to all.

Key Terms
السفر الخامس
بني إخوة
بني إسماعيل
نبياً مثلك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the 'prophet like Moses' in Deuteronomy refers to Joshua or another Israelite prophet from the same lineage.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that 'brethren of Israel' means the Children of Ishmael, not a prophet from within Israel. The prophet must come from a different lineage, which is exactly Muhammad's lineage.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's interpretation, to whom does the phrase 'their brethren' (بني إخوة) refer in the Torah prophecy?
A) The Edomites
B) The Children of Ishmael
C) The Egyptians
D) The Jews

Key Takeaway
Sanusi uses a Torah prophecy to argue that Muhammad is the promised prophet like Moses, based on lineage and historical fulfillment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This prophecy comes from a scripture you believe has been altered. Yet the author uses it as proof. How does that challenge you to re-examine your attitude toward previous scriptures? Do you see them as completely false or as containing remnants of truth? What does your response say about your trust in Allah's preservation of His message?
?
The prophecy describes a prophet 'like Moses'. Reflect on the similarities between Moses and Muhammad — both brought laws, faced opposition, and led communities. How does seeing this pattern strengthen your conviction in Muhammad's prophethood? Have you ever personally compared their stories to see God's consistent method?
?
The warning: 'I will take vengeance on him who does not heed' applies to everyone who hears the prophet's message. Are you truly heeding the words of Muhammad? Is there an area of your life where you are ignoring or downplaying his commands? What will you change today to take this warning seriously?
